│  │  - Invocation count, duration, errors                      │   │
│  │  - Custom metrics and alarms                               │   │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Typical Flow for anihpj Job Portal:
1. User creates job post → DynamoDB Stream triggers Lambda
2. Lambda processes job data, extracts skills/location
3. Lambda queries RDS for matching candidates
4. Lambda sends email notifications via SES
5. Lambda logs results to CloudWatch
6. All done in seconds, no servers to manage!

🔧 Core Concepts

⚡ Lambda Functions

A Lambda function is the fundamental unit of Lambda. It contains your code and configuration that defines how Lambda processes events.

📊 Lambda Function Anatomy
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              AWS LAMBDA FUNCTION STRUCTURE                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                              │
│  Function Name: anihpj-job-notifier                         │
│  Runtime: Python 3.12                                        │
│  Handler: lambda_function.lambda_handler                     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Function Code (lambda_function.py)                │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │  import json                                       │     │
│  │  import boto3                                      │     │
│  │  import os                                         │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │  def lambda_handler(event, context):               │     │
│  │      """Main entry point"""                        │     │
│  │      # event = input data from trigger            │     │
│  │      # context = runtime information              │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      print(f"Processing: {event}")                │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      # Your business logic here                   │     │
│  │      result = process_job_post(event)             │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      return {                                      │     │
│  │          'statusCode': 200,                        │     │
│  │          'body': json.dumps(result)               │     │
│  │      }                                             │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Configuration                                      │     │
│  │  ├─ Memory: 512 MB (128 MB - 10,240 MB)           │     │
│  │  ├─ Timeout: 30 seconds (max 15 minutes)          │     │
│  │  ├─ Environment Variables:                         │     │
│  │  │   • DB_HOST=anihpj-db.amazonaws.com            │     │
│  │  │   • DB_PASSWORD=         │     │
│  │  │   • SES_SENDER=noreply@anihpj.com              │     │
│  │  ├─ IAM Execution Role: anihpj-lambda-role        │     │
│  │  ├─ VPC: vpc-12345 (if RDS access needed)         │     │
│  │  └─ Layers: [django-utils-layer, psycopg2-layer]  │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Triggers (Event Sources)                          │     │
│  │  ├─ API Gateway (HTTP POST /jobs)                  │     │
│  │  ├─ EventBridge (Schedule: rate(1 hour))           │     │
│  │  ├─ S3 (Object created in anihpj-uploads/)         │     │
│  │  └─ DynamoDB Stream (Jobs table changes)           │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Destinations (On Success/Failure)                 │     │
│  │  ├─ Success → SQS queue for further processing    │     │
│  │  └─ Failure → SNS topic for alerts                │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🚀 Invocation Types

Lambda supports three invocation types, each suited for different use cases:

📡 Three Lambda Invocation Models
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    INVOCATION TYPES                            │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  1️⃣ SYNCHRONOUS (Request-Response)                            │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Client → Lambda → Processing → Response → Client    │    │
│  │          ↓                            ↑               │    │
│  │          └────── Waits for result ────┘               │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • API Gateway requests (REST APIs)                            │
│  • Mobile/web app direct invocations                           │
│  • Real-time data transformations                              │
│  • User-facing operations (must wait for response)             │
│                                                                │
│  Example: GET /api/jobs/{id}                                   │
│  Client waits for job details to be returned                   │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Client responsible                                     │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  2️⃣ ASYNCHRONOUS (Fire-and-Forget)                            │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Client → Lambda → 202 Accepted                       │    │
│  │              ↓                                        │    │
│  │              └─→ Queue → Process → Done               │    │
│  │                   (happens later)                     │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • S3 events (file uploaded → process later)                   │
│  • SNS/EventBridge triggers                                    │
│  • Background tasks (email sending, reports)                   │
│  • Non-critical operations (can delay response)                │
│                                                                │
│  Example: S3 file upload → Lambda processes image              │
│  User doesn't wait for processing to complete                  │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Automatic (2 times by Lambda)                          │
│  Dead Letter Queue: Can configure for failed invocations       │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  3️⃣ POLL-BASED (Event Source Mapping)                         │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Lambda polls → SQS/Kinesis → Fetches batch          │    │
│  │                    ↓                                  │    │
│  │                    Process batch → ACK/NACK           │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • SQS queues (batch message processing)                       │
│  • Kinesis/DynamoDB Streams (stream processing)                │
│  • Kafka topics (MSK integration)                              │
│  • High-throughput event processing                            │
│                                                                │
│  Example: SQS queue with 1000 job application messages         │
│  Lambda processes in batches of 10                             │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Depends on source (SQS: message visibility)            │
│  Batch Size: Configurable (1-10,000 for SQS)                   │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

For anihpj Job Portal:
✓ Synchronous: REST API endpoints (search jobs, get details)
✓ Asynchronous: Email notifications, report generation
✓ Poll-based: Process application queue, analytics pipeline
📡 Event Sources (Triggers)

Lambda functions are triggered by events from various AWS services. Here are the most common event sources for Django applications:

🎯 Common Event Sources for anihpj
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│               EVENT SOURCES & USE CASES                        │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  📬 API GATEWAY (HTTP/REST APIs)                               │
│  ├─ Invocation: Synchronous                                    │
│  ├─ Use Case: RESTful API backend for mobile/web              │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      GET  /api/jobs → Lambda lists jobs                        │
│      POST /api/jobs → Lambda creates job post                  │
│      PUT  /api/jobs/{id} → Lambda updates job                  │
│                                                                │
│  📦 S3 (Object Events)                                         │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Triggers: s3:ObjectCreated, s3:ObjectRemoved              │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Upload resume.pdf → Lambda processes & extracts text      │
│      Upload company-logo.png → Lambda creates thumbnails       │
│                                                                │
│  📨 SQS (Message Queues)                                       │
│  ├─ Invocation: Poll-based (Event Source Mapping)             │
│  ├─ Batch Size: 1-10 messages per invocation                  │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Job applications queue → Lambda sends notifications       │
│      Email sending queue → Lambda dispatches via SES           │
│                                                                │
│  🔔 SNS (Pub/Sub Notifications)                                │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Fan-out: One message → Multiple Lambdas                    │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      New job posted → SNS topic → Lambda notifies subscribers  │
│                                                                │
│  ⏰ EventBridge (Scheduled Events)                             │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Schedule: Cron expressions or rate expressions            │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      rate(1 hour) → Lambda cleans up expired job posts         │
│      cron(0 9 * * ? *) → Lambda sends daily digest at 9 AM    │
│                                                                │
│  💾 DynamoDB Streams                                           │
│  ├─ Invocation: Poll-based (Event Source Mapping)             │
│  ├─ Change Data Capture: INSERT, MODIFY, REMOVE               │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Job post created → Stream → Lambda updates search index   │
│      Application submitted → Stream → Lambda triggers workflow │
│                                                                │
│  🗄️ RDS Events (via EventBridge)                               │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Events: DB instance events, automated backups             │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      DB snapshot completed → Lambda verifies backup integrity  │
│                                                                │
│  📊 CloudWatch Logs                                            │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Trigger: Log patterns matching                            │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Error log detected → Lambda sends alert to Slack          │
│                                                                │
│  🔗 Application Load Balancer (ALB)                            │
│  ├─ Invocation: Synchronous                                    │
│  ├─ Use Case: Alternative to API Gateway                       │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      ALB target group → Lambda handles HTTP requests           │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🏗️ Execution Environment

Understanding Lambda's execution environment is crucial for building efficient functions.

🔄 Lambda Execution Lifecycle
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            LAMBDA EXECUTION ENVIRONMENT LIFECYCLE              │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  PHASE 1: INIT (Cold Start) - Happens once per container      │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  1. Download function code from S3                    │    │
│  │  2. Start execution environment (container)           │    │
│  │  3. Initialize runtime (Python 3.12)                  │    │
│  │  4. Load layers (if any)                              │    │
│  │  5. Execute INIT code (outside handler)               │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │     # Code outside handler runs ONCE                  │    │
│  │     import boto3                                      │    │
│  │     db_client = boto3.client('rds-data')  # Reused!  │    │
│  │     s3_client = boto3.client('s3')         # Reused!  │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │  Duration: 100ms - 2000ms (variable)                  │    │
│  │  Billed: Yes (since January 2024)                     │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  PHASE 2: INVOKE (Warm Execution) - Runs for each request     │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  1. Lambda receives event                             │    │
│  │  2. Execute handler function                          │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │     def lambda_handler(event, context):               │    │
│  │         # This runs for EVERY invocation             │    │
│  │         job_data = event['body']                     │    │
│  │         result = process_job(job_data)               │    │
│  │         return response                               │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │  3. Return response                                   │    │
│  │  Duration: Your function execution time               │    │
│  │  Billed: Yes (per ms of execution)                    │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                     │                                          │
│                     ▼                                          │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Container stays warm for ~5-15 minutes               │    │
│  │  (Next invocation = no INIT phase = faster!)          │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                     │                                          │
│                     ▼                                          │
│  PHASE 3: SHUTDOWN (If no requests)                           │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Container destroyed after idle timeout                │    │
│  │  Next invocation = Cold Start again                    │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  OPTIMIZATION TIP:                                             │
│  ✓ Initialize connections OUTSIDE handler (reused across)     │
│  ✓ Use /tmp for temporary files (512 MB - 10 GB available)    │
│  ✓ Reuse container state between invocations                   │
│  ✗ Don't assume container persists (may be destroyed anytime)  │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
💻 Cold Start vs. Warm Start Example
# lambda_function.py
import json
import boto3
import psycopg2
import os

# ============================================
# INIT PHASE CODE (Runs once per container)
# ============================================
print("INIT: Initializing connections...")

# These clients are created once and reused!
s3_client = boto3.client('s3')
ses_client = boto3.client('ses')

# Database connection (reused for warm starts)
DB_CONFIG = {
    'host': os.environ['DB_HOST'],
    'database': 'anihpj',
    'user': os.environ['DB_USER'],
    'password': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD']
}

# Don't open connection here! 
# Open when needed, connection pooling recommended
print("INIT: Configuration loaded")

# ============================================
# INVOKE PHASE CODE (Runs every invocation)
# ============================================
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """
    Handler function - executes for every request
    Duration impacts cost directly
    """
    print("INVOKE: Processing request...")
    
    # Parse incoming job post data
    job_data = json.loads(event['body'])
    
    # Connect to database (with retry logic)
    conn = psycopg2.connect(**DB_CONFIG)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    try:
        # Insert job post into anihpj database
        cursor.execute("""
            INSERT INTO jobpost_jobpost 
            (title, description, company, location, salary_min, salary_max)
            VALUES (%s, %s, %s, %s, %s, %s)
            RETURNING id
        """, (
            job_data['title'],
            job_data['description'],
            job_data['company'],
            job_data['location'],
            job_data['salary_min'],
            job_data['salary_max']
        ))
        
        job_id = cursor.fetchone()[0]
        conn.commit()
        
        # Send notification email via SES (non-blocking)
        ses_client.send_email(
            Source='noreply@anihpj.com',
            Destination={'ToAddresses': ['admin@anihpj.com']},
            Message={
                'Subject': {'Data': f'New Job Posted: {job_data["title"]}'},
                'Body': {'Text': {'Data': f'Job ID: {job_id}'}}
            }
        )
        
        return {
            'statusCode': 201,
            'headers': {'Content-Type': 'application/json'},
            'body': json.dumps({
                'message': 'Job created successfully',
                'job_id': job_id
            })
        }
        
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"ERROR: {str(e)}")
        conn.rollback()
        return {
            'statusCode': 500,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': str(e)})
        }
        
    finally:
        cursor.close()
        conn.close()

# Execution Times:
# Cold Start: INIT (500ms) + INVOKE (200ms) = 700ms total
# Warm Start: INVOKE (200ms) only = 200ms total
# Savings: 71% faster on warm starts!

🚀 Getting Started with Lambda

Before creating your first Lambda function for anihpj:

✅ AWS Account Setup
   • Active AWS account with billing enabled
   • IAM user with Lambda permissions
   • AWS CLI installed and configured

   • Python 3.9+ installed locally
   • Code editor (VS Code recommended)
   • Git for version control

✅ Knowledge Requirements
   • Basic Python programming
   • Understanding of Django models
   • Familiarity with AWS console
🎯 Create First Function
Simple Lambda for anihpj Job Notifications
import json
import boto3
from datetime import datetime

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """Send job notification email via SES"""
    
    job_data = json.loads(event['body'])
    ses_client = boto3.client('ses')
    
    ses_client.send_email(
        Source='noreply@anihpj.com',
        Destination={'ToAddresses': [job_data['subscriber_email']]},
        Message={
            'Subject': {'Data': f"New Job: {job_data['title']}"},
            'Body': {'Text': {'Data': f"Check out this opportunity at {job_data['company']}"}}
        }
    )
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Email sent'}
🧪 Testing & Debugging
💡 Quick Testing: Use AWS Console test events, AWS SAM CLI for local testing, or CloudWatch Logs for debugging production issues.

🔑 Key Features

⚡ Triggers & Event Sources

Lambda integrates with 200+ AWS services. Common triggers for anihpj: API Gateway (REST APIs), S3 (file uploads), EventBridge (scheduled tasks), SQS (message queues), DynamoDB Streams (data changes).

📦 Lambda Layers

Package dependencies separately from code. Create layers for common libraries (psycopg2, Django, boto3) and reuse across multiple functions. Max 5 layers per function, 250 MB total size limit.

🔧 Environment Variables
import os

# Access environment variables
db_host = os.environ['DB_HOST']
db_password = os.environ['DB_PASSWORD']

# Best practice: Use Secrets Manager for sensitive data
import boto3
secrets = boto3.client('secretsmanager')
secret = secrets.get_secret_value(SecretId='anihpj/db-password')
password = json.loads(secret['SecretString'])['password']
🌐 VPC Configuration

Connect Lambda to VPC for RDS database access. Configure subnets (use private), security groups, and ensure NAT Gateway or VPC Endpoints for internet access. Note: VPC increases cold start time by 1-2 seconds.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

💵 Pricing Model
Lambda Pricing (2025):
• Requests: First 1M/month FREE, then $0.20 per 1M
• Compute: 400,000 GB-seconds/month FREE, then $0.0000166667 per GB-second
• Formula: (Memory in GB) × (Duration in seconds) = GB-seconds

Example: 1M requests, 512 MB, 200ms each
• Requests: FREE (within 1M limit)
• Compute: 1M × 0.5 GB × 0.2s = 100,000 GB-seconds → FREE
• Total: $0.00 🎉
💡 Cost Optimization
Top Optimization Strategies:
✅ Right-size memory (use Lambda Power Tuning tool)
✅ Reduce execution time (optimize code, reuse connections)
✅ Use Graviton2 (ARM64) for 20% cost savings
✅ Batch processing (10 messages/invocation vs 1)
✅ Minimize package size (faster cold starts)
✅ Use asynchronous invocation for non-critical tasks
✅ Monitor with CloudWatch, set cost alarms
📊 Cost Calculator
💡 Estimate: For anihpj with 5M requests/month, 512MB, 300ms avg duration: ~$25/month. Use AWS Pricing Calculator for precise estimates.

📈 Performance & Scalability

🔄 Concurrency & Scaling
Lambda Concurrency:
• Default: 1000 concurrent executions per region (soft limit)
• Automatic scaling: 0 to 1000s in seconds
• Reserved concurrency: Guarantee capacity for critical functions
• Provisioned concurrency: Pre-warm containers (eliminates cold starts)

For anihpj:
• Peak traffic: 100 requests/second
• Avg duration: 300ms
• Concurrent executions needed: 100 × 0.3 = 30
• Well within limits! ✓
❄️ Cold Starts
Cold Start Optimization:
• Cold start: ~500ms-2000ms (first invocation)
• Warm start: <10ms (subsequent invocations)

Mitigation Strategies:
✅ Keep functions warm with scheduled pings (EventBridge every 5 min)
✅ Use Provisioned Concurrency for critical endpoints
✅ Minimize package size (< 10 MB)
✅ Initialize connections outside handler
✅ Use Graviton2 (faster startup)
✅ Avoid VPC if possible (adds 1-2s to cold start)
⚡ Performance Tuning
# Performance Best Practices for anihpj Lambda

# 1. Initialize outside handler (reused across invocations)
import boto3
import psycopg2

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')  # ✅ Reused
db_conn_pool = create_connection_pool()  # ✅ Reused

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # 2. Use connection pooling
    conn = db_conn_pool.getconn()
    
    # 3. Parallel processing with threads
    from concurrent.futures import ThreadPoolExecutor
    with ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=10) as executor:
        results = executor.map(process_job, job_list)
    
    # 4. Use async/await for I/O operations
    import asyncio
    results = await asyncio.gather(*[fetch_data(url) for url in urls])
    
    # 5. Cache frequently accessed data
    cached_data = get_from_cache() or fetch_and_cache()
    
    db_conn_pool.putconn(conn)
    return {'statusCode': 200}

🎓 Advanced Topics

🐳 Container Images

Deploy Lambda functions as container images (up to 10 GB). Supports custom base images, easier local testing, familiar Docker workflow. Ideal for functions with large dependencies.

🔌 Lambda Extensions

Integrate monitoring tools (Datadog, New Relic), secrets fetching, logging without code changes. Extensions run in separate processes alongside your function.

⚙️ Provisioned Concurrency

Pre-warm execution environments to eliminate cold starts. Critical for latency-sensitive APIs. Cost: $0.000004167 per GB-second (on top of regular pricing). Use for peak hours only to optimize costs.

🎯 Destinations

Route function results to SQS, SNS, EventBridge, or another Lambda automatically. Separate success and failure destinations. Better than manual error handling for async workflows.

⚙️ Setup & Configuration
# Django in Lambda - anihpj example

# 1. Install Django in Lambda Layer
# pip install Django psycopg2-binary -t python/

# 2. Lambda function with Django ORM
import os
import django
from django.conf import settings

# Configure Django settings
os.environ.setdefault('DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE', 'anihpj.settings')
settings.configure(
    DATABASES={
        'default': {
            'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
            'NAME': os.environ['DB_NAME'],
            'USER': os.environ['DB_USER'],
            'PASSWORD': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD'],
            'HOST': os.environ['DB_HOST'],
            'PORT': '5432',
        }
    },
    INSTALLED_APPS=['jobpost'],
)
django.setup()

# 3. Use Django models in Lambda
from jobpost.models import JobPost, Skills

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Query using Django ORM
    python_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
        skills__name='Python',
        is_active=True
    ).select_related('location', 'author')
    
    results = [
        {
            'id': job.id,
            'title': job.title,
            'company': job.company,
            'location': str(job.location),
        }
        for job in python_jobs[:10]
    ]
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': json.dumps(results)}

✨ Best Practices

🔒 Security Checklist
Lambda Security Best Practices:

✅ IAM & Access Control
   • Principle of least privilege for execution roles
   • Use resource-based policies for cross-account access
   • Enable MFA for sensitive operations
   • Regular IAM policy audits

✅ Secrets Management
   • NEVER hardcode credentials in code
   • Use AWS Secrets Manager or Parameter Store
   • Rotate secrets regularly (automated)
   • Environment variables encrypted at rest

✅ Network Security
   • VPC for private resource access
   • Security groups with minimal ports
   • Use VPC Endpoints (avoid public internet)
   • Enable VPC Flow Logs

✅ Code Security
   • Input validation (prevent injection attacks)
   • Output encoding (prevent XSS)
   • Dependency scanning (npm audit, safety)
   • Regular security updates

✅ Monitoring & Audit
   • Enable CloudTrail for audit logs
   • CloudWatch Logs for function execution
   • Set up alarms for anomalies
   • Regular security reviews
💻 Code Best Practices
# Lambda Code Best Practices

# ✅ GOOD: Separate handler from business logic
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """Handler delegates to business logic"""
    try:
        result = process_job_application(event)
        return success_response(result)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Error: {str(e)}")
        return error_response(str(e))

def process_job_application(event):
    """Pure business logic - easy to test"""
    job_data = parse_event(event)
    validate_job_data(job_data)
    save_to_database(job_data)
    return {'job_id': job_data['id']}

# ✅ GOOD: Use structured logging
import logging
import json

logger = logging.getLogger()
logger.setLevel(logging.INFO)

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    logger.info(json.dumps({
        'event': 'job_created',
        'job_id': event['job_id'],
        'user_id': event['user_id'],
        'timestamp': datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
    }))

# ✅ GOOD: Implement idempotency
import hashlib

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Generate idempotency key
    event_hash = hashlib.md5(json.dumps(event, sort_keys=True).encode()).hexdigest()
    
    # Check if already processed
    if check_processed(event_hash):
        return cached_response(event_hash)
    
    result = process_event(event)
    cache_result(event_hash, result)
    return result

# ✅ GOOD: Graceful error handling
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    try:
        return process_request(event)
    except ValidationError as e:
        return {
            'statusCode': 400,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': 'Invalid input', 'details': str(e)})
        }
    except DatabaseError as e:
        logger.error(f"DB Error: {str(e)}")
        return {
            'statusCode': 500,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': 'Internal server error'})
        }
    except Exception as e:
        logger.critical(f"Unexpected error: {str(e)}")
        raise  # Let Lambda retry
📊 Monitoring & Logging
Monitoring Strategy for anihpj Lambda:

CloudWatch Metrics:
• Invocations: Total function executions
• Duration: Average, Min, Max execution time
• Errors: Failed invocations
• Throttles: Concurrent execution limit reached
• ConcurrentExecutions: Active instances

CloudWatch Alarms:
✓ Error rate > 1% → Alert via SNS
✓ Duration > 10s → Performance degradation
✓ Throttles > 0 → Need concurrency increase
✓ Cost > $100/day → Budget alert

X-Ray Tracing:
✓ End-to-end request tracing
✓ Identify bottlenecks
✓ Service map visualization
✓ Performance insights

Custom Metrics:
• Business metrics (jobs created, emails sent)
• Application-specific errors
• User journey tracking
⚠️ Error Handling
# Comprehensive Error Handling

class LambdaError(Exception):
    """Base exception for Lambda functions"""
    pass

class RetryableError(LambdaError):
    """Error that should trigger retry"""
    pass

class NonRetryableError(LambdaError):
    """Error that should not retry"""
    pass

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    try:
        return process_event(event)
    
    except RetryableError as e:
        # Let Lambda retry automatically
        logger.warning(f"Retryable error: {str(e)}")
        raise
    
    except NonRetryableError as e:
        # Don't retry, send to DLQ
        logger.error(f"Non-retryable error: {str(e)}")
        send_to_dlq(event, str(e))
        return {'statusCode': 400, 'error': str(e)}
    
    except Exception as e:
        # Unknown error - log and retry
        logger.critical(f"Unexpected error: {str(e)}", exc_info=True)
        raise

# Configure Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)
# AWS Console → Lambda → Configuration → Asynchronous invocation
# Set DLQ: SQS queue or SNS topic for failed events

PUT    /api/jobs/{id}     → Update job
DELETE /api/jobs/{id}     → Delete job
POST   /api/jobs/{id}/apply → Submit application

Benefits:
✓ Auto-scaling (handle traffic spikes)
✓ Pay-per-request (no idle costs)
✓ Built-in HTTPS (via API Gateway)
✓ CORS support
✓ API keys, throttling, caching

Scheduled Tasks with EventBridge:

cron(0 2 * * ? *)  → Daily cleanup (expired jobs)
cron(0 9 * * MON *)→ Weekly digest email
rate(1 hour)       → Hourly job index refresh
rate(5 minutes)    → Health checks & monitoring

Benefits:
✓ No servers to maintain
✓ Reliable execution
✓ Cost-effective (only run when needed)
✓ Easy to modify schedules

🔧 Troubleshooting

⚠️ Common Issues
1. Timeout Errors
   Symptom: "Task timed out after X seconds"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Increase timeout (max 15 minutes)
   ✓ Optimize code (reduce execution time)
   ✓ Use asynchronous processing
   ✓ Break into smaller functions

2. Out of Memory
   Symptom: "Process exited before completing request"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Increase memory allocation
   ✓ Process data in batches
   ✓ Use generators instead of lists
   ✓ Monitor memory usage with CloudWatch

3. Cold Start Latency
   Symptom: First request slow (>2 seconds)
   Solutions:
   ✓ Use Provisioned Concurrency
   ✓ Reduce package size
   ✓ Keep functions warm (scheduled pings)
   ✓ Initialize outside handler

4. VPC Connectivity Issues
   Symptom: Can't connect to RDS or internet
   Solutions:
   ✓ Check security group rules
   ✓ Verify subnet configuration
   ✓ Add NAT Gateway for internet
   ✓ Use VPC Endpoints for AWS services

5. Permission Errors
   Symptom: "AccessDeniedException"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Check IAM execution role
   ✓ Verify resource policies
   ✓ Review CloudTrail logs
   ✓ Test with elevated permissions first
🐛 Debugging Strategies
# Debugging Tools & Techniques

# 1. CloudWatch Logs Insights
# Query: Parse JSON logs, find errors
fields @timestamp, @message
| filter @message like /ERROR/
| sort @timestamp desc
| limit 20

# 2. AWS X-Ray Tracing
import aws_xray_sdk
from aws_xray_sdk.core import xray_recorder

@xray_recorder.capture('process_job')
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Trace execution, find bottlenecks
    pass

# 3. Local Testing with SAM
# sam local invoke anihpj-job-processor --event test-event.json

# 4. Print Debugging (structured logging)
import json
import logging

logger = logging.getLogger()
logger.setLevel(logging.DEBUG)

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    logger.debug(f"Event received: {json.dumps(event)}")
    logger.info(f"Processing job ID: {event['job_id']}")
    # ...
    logger.debug(f"Result: {json.dumps(result)}")
❓ Frequently Asked Questions
Q: Can I run Django admin in Lambda?
A: Not recommended. Django admin requires persistent server. Use EC2 or ECS for admin interface. Lambda for APIs and background tasks only.

Q: How do I handle database connections?
A: Use connection pooling, initialize outside handler, use RDS Proxy for better connection management.

Q: What's the max execution time?
A: 15 minutes. For longer tasks, use Step Functions to chain multiple Lambdas.

Q: How many concurrent executions can I have?
A: Default 1000 per region (soft limit). Request increase via AWS Support if needed.

Q: Can Lambda access my VPC resources?
A: Yes, configure VPC, subnets, and security groups in Lambda settings.

Q: How do I deploy Lambda functions?
A: AWS Console, AWS CLI, AWS SAM, Serverless Framework, Terraform, CloudFormation.

Q: Can I use custom Python packages?
A: Yes, include in deployment package or use Lambda Layers. Binary dependencies may need special builds for Amazon Linux 2.

Q: How do I reduce cold starts?
A: Provisioned Concurrency, smaller packages, Graviton2, keep warm with scheduled pings.

⌨️ API & CLI Reference

🖥️ AWS CLI Commands
# Create Lambda function
aws lambda create-function \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --runtime python3.12 \
    --role arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/lambda-execution-role \
    --handler lambda_function.lambda_handler \
    --zip-file fileb://function.zip \
    --environment Variables="{DB_HOST=anihpj-db.amazonaws.com,DB_NAME=anihpj}"

# Invoke function
aws lambda invoke \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --payload '{"job_id": 123, "email": "user@example.com"}' \
    response.json

# Update function code
aws lambda update-function-code \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --zip-file fileb://new-version.zip

# Get function configuration
aws lambda get-function-configuration \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier

# List functions
aws lambda list-functions

# View CloudWatch logs
aws logs tail /aws/lambda/anihpj-job-notifier --follow
🐍 Boto3 SDK (Python)
import boto3
import json

lambda_client = boto3.client('lambda')

# Invoke Lambda function synchronously
response = lambda_client.invoke(
    FunctionName='anihpj-job-notifier',
    InvocationType='RequestResponse',
    Payload=json.dumps({
        'job_id': 123,
        'subscriber_email': 'user@example.com'
    })
)

result = json.loads(response['Payload'].read())
print(result)

# Invoke asynchronously (fire-and-forget)
lambda_client.invoke(
    FunctionName='anihpj-job-notifier',
    InvocationType='Event',
    Payload=json.dumps({'job_id': 456})
)

# Create function
lambda_client.create_function(
    FunctionName='anihpj-new-function',
    Runtime='python3.12',
    Role='arn:aws:iam::123:role/lambda-role',
    Handler='lambda_function.lambda_handler',
    Code={'ZipFile': open('function.zip', 'rb').read()},
    Environment={'Variables': {'DB_HOST': 'localhost'}}
)
📦 SAM & Serverless Framework
# SAM template.yaml
AWSTemplateFormatVersion: '2010-09-09'
Transform: AWS::Serverless-2016-10-31

Resources:
  AnihpjJobNotifier:
    Type: AWS::Serverless::Function
    Properties:
      FunctionName: anihpj-job-notifier
      Runtime: python3.12
      Handler: lambda_function.lambda_handler
      CodeUri: ./src
      MemorySize: 512
      Timeout: 30
      Environment:
        Variables:
          DB_HOST: !Ref DatabaseHost
          S3_BUCKET: !Ref UploadBucket
      Events:
        ApiEvent:
          Type: Api
          Properties:
            Path: /notify
            Method: post

# Deploy
# sam build
# sam deploy --guided

🔗 AWS Service Integration

🚪 API Gateway
Lambda + API Gateway = Serverless REST API

Integration Types:
• Lambda Proxy: Event includes HTTP request details
• Lambda Non-Proxy: Custom request/response transformation

Example Lambda Response for API Gateway:
{
  "statusCode": 200,
  "headers": {
    "Content-Type": "application/json",
    "Access-Control-Allow-Origin": "*"
  },
  "body": "{\"message\": \"Success\"}"
}

Benefits:
✓ Auto-scaling
✓ CORS support
✓ API keys & usage plans
✓ Request throttling
✓ Caching
💾 DynamoDB Integration
DynamoDB Streams → Lambda

Use Case: Real-time data processing
• Job post created → Update search index
• Application submitted → Trigger notification
• User profile updated → Sync to analytics

Event Structure:
{
  "Records": [{
    "eventName": "INSERT",
    "dynamodb": {
      "NewImage": {"job_id": {"N": "123"}, ...}
    }
  }]
}
📦 S3 Events
S3 → Lambda

Triggers:
• s3:ObjectCreated:* (file upload)
• s3:ObjectRemoved:* (file delete)

Use Cases:
• Resume upload → Parse & extract text
• Image upload → Create thumbnails
• CSV upload → Process & import data

Configuration:
S3 Bucket → Properties → Event notifications → Add Lambda trigger
📨 SQS Queues
SQS → Lambda (Event Source Mapping)

Benefits:
• Batch processing (1-10 messages per invocation)
• Automatic retries
• Dead Letter Queue for failed messages
• Throttle protection

Configuration:
Lambda → Add trigger → SQS → Select queue
Batch size: 10
Batch window: 5 seconds

Use Case: Email notification queue
100 messages → Lambda processes in 10 batches of 10

   ✓ Reusable constructs
🔄 CI/CD Pipelines
# GitHub Actions example
name: Deploy Lambda

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Setup Python
        uses: actions/setup-python@v4
        with:
          python-version: '3.12'
      
      - name: Install dependencies
        run: |
          pip install -r requirements.txt -t package/
          cp lambda_function.py package/
          cd package && zip -r ../function.zip .
      
      - name: Deploy to Lambda
        env:
          AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
          AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        run: |
          aws lambda update-function-code \
            --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
            --zip-file fileb://function.zip \
            --region us-east-1

📖 Glossary

Key AWS Lambda Terms:

Cold Start
    Initial startup time when Lambda creates a new execution environment.
    Includes downloading code, starting runtime, and running init code.

Concurrency
    Number of function instances processing events simultaneously.
    Default limit: 1000 per region (can be increased).

Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)
    SQS queue or SNS topic for failed asynchronous invocations.
    Used for debugging and reprocessing failed events.

Destination
    Target service (SQS, SNS, EventBridge, Lambda) for function results.
    Separate destinations for success and failure outcomes.

Event Source
    AWS service or application that triggers Lambda function execution.
    Examples: S3, API Gateway, DynamoDB, SQS, EventBridge.

Event Source Mapping
    Configuration that reads from streams/queues and invokes Lambda.
    Used for Kinesis, DynamoDB Streams, SQS, Kafka.

Execution Environment
    Secure, isolated runtime where Lambda function code executes.
    Reused across invocations for performance (warm starts).

Execution Role
    IAM role that grants Lambda permission to access AWS services.
    Required for all Lambda functions.

Function
    Serverless application component containing code and configuration.
    Basic unit of deployment and scaling in Lambda.

Handler
    Entry point method that Lambda calls to execute your code.
    Format: filename.method_name (e.g., lambda_function.lambda_handler)

Invocation
    Single execution of a Lambda function in response to an event.
    Charged per invocation and compute time.

Lambda Layer
    ZIP archive containing libraries, dependencies, or custom runtimes.
    Shared across multiple functions to reduce package size.

Provisioned Concurrency
    Pre-initialized execution environments that eliminate cold starts.
    Additional cost but provides consistent low latency.

Reserved Concurrency
    Maximum number of concurrent instances for a specific function.
    Guarantees capacity and prevents function from consuming all account concurrency.

Runtime
    Language-specific environment for executing Lambda functions.
    Examples: Python 3.12, Node.js 20.x, Java 17, .NET 8, Go 1.x

Timeout
    Maximum time a function can run before Lambda terminates it.
    Range: 1 second to 15 minutes (900 seconds).

Trigger
    Resource or configuration that invokes Lambda function automatically.
    Examples: S3 bucket, API Gateway endpoint, CloudWatch Events rule.

Warm Start
    Fast execution when Lambda reuses existing execution environment.
    No cold start overhead, typically <10ms initialization.

X-Ray
    AWS service for tracing and analyzing Lambda function performance.
    Provides insights into execution time, downstream calls, and bottlenecks.

📝 Changelog & Version History

AWS Lambda Major Updates (Recent):

2024-2025
─────────
• November 2024: Python 3.13 runtime support
• October 2024: Increased ephemeral storage up to 10 GB
• September 2024: Lambda SnapStart for Java improvements
• August 2024: Enhanced CloudWatch Logs integration
• July 2024: Advanced Logging Controls (JSON format)
• June 2024: Lambda response streaming for Node.js
• May 2024: IPv6 support for VPC Lambda functions
• April 2024: Lambda Telemetry API improvements
• March 2024: Graviton3 processors (20% better performance)
• February 2024: Faster cold starts for Graviton2
• January 2024: Init phase billing changes

2023
────
• Q4: Lambda response payload streaming (HTTP 200 OK chunks)
• Q4: Node.js 20.x runtime support
• Q3: Recursive loop detection and protection
• Q3: Python 3.11 runtime support
• Q2: Lambda SnapStart (Java 11/17 - instant cold starts)
• Q2: Function URLs with IAM authentication
• Q1: Maximum timeout increased to 15 minutes
• Q1: Lambda Extensions API enhancements

2022
────
• Q4: ARM64 architecture (Graviton2) cost reduction
• Q3: Event Filtering for S3, DynamoDB, Kinesis
• Q2: Lambda Function URLs (built-in HTTPS endpoints)
• Q1: Document DB event source support
• Q1: Increased deployment package size to 250 MB

2021
────
• Q4: Support for container images up to 10 GB
• Q3: Lambda@Edge improvements (1 MB function size)
• Q2: Python 3.9 runtime support
• Q1: Provisioned Concurrency for container images

Runtime Evolution:
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Python:  2.7 → 3.6 → 3.7 → 3.8 → 3.9 → 3.10 → 3.11 → 3.12 → 3.13 │
│ Node.js: 8.x → 10.x → 12.x → 14.x → 16.x → 18.x → 20.x      │
│ Java:    8 → 11 → 17 → 21                                    │
│ .NET:    Core 2.1 → 3.1 → 6 → 7 → 8                         │
│ Go:      1.x (custom runtime)                                 │
│ Ruby:    2.7 → 3.2 → 3.3                                     │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Key Feature Milestones:
• 2025: Multi-region active-active deployments
• 2024: Cold start optimizations (50% reduction)
• 2023: SnapStart (near-zero cold starts for Java)
• 2022: Function URLs (native HTTP endpoints)
• 2021: Container image support (up to 10 GB)
• 2020: Provisioned Concurrency (predictable performance)
• 2019: Destinations (automatic result routing)
• 2018: Lambda Layers (shared dependencies)
• 2017: Environment variables, VPC improvements
• 2016: Dead Letter Queues, versioning & aliases
• 2015: Scheduled events (cron jobs)
• 2014: AWS Lambda launched (Node.js only)

For anihpj Job Portal:
• Recommended: Use Python 3.12 runtime (latest stable)
• Architecture: ARM64 (Graviton2/3) for 20% cost savings
• Features: Use Layers for Django dependencies
• Monitoring: Enable X-Ray tracing and CloudWatch Logs Insights
• Cold Starts: Consider Provisioned Concurrency for critical APIs
• Updates: Stay on supported runtimes (AWS deprecates old versions)

⚖️ When to Use Lambda vs EC2 for anihpj

📊 Decision Matrix
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            LAMBDA vs EC2 FOR ANIHPJ JOB PORTAL                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  USE LAMBDA FOR:                                               │
│  ✅ Background Tasks                                            │
│     • Send email notifications (new job posts)                 │
│     • Process resume uploads (PDF → text extraction)           │
│     • Generate daily/weekly reports                            │
│     • Cleanup expired job posts (scheduled)                    │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ REST API Endpoints (with API Gateway)                       │
│     • Job search API (GET /api/jobs?skills=python)            │
│     • Job details API (GET /api/jobs/{id})                     │
│     • Application submission (POST /api/jobs/{id}/apply)       │
│     • User profile updates                                     │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Event-Driven Processing                                     │
│     • S3 file upload → Process company logo                    │
│     • DynamoDB change → Update search index                    │
│     • SQS queue → Batch email sending                          │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Scheduled Tasks (Cron Jobs)                                 │
│     • Daily: Close expired job posts                           │
│     • Weekly: Send digest emails to subscribers                │
│     • Hourly: Refresh job recommendations                      │
│     • Monthly: Generate analytics reports                      │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Microservices Architecture                                  │
│     • Independent scaling per service                          │
│     • Pay only for actual usage                                │
│     • Rapid deployment and updates                             │
│                                                                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  USE EC2 FOR:                                                  │
│  ✅ Main Django Web Application                                 │
│     • Django admin interface                                   │
│     • Complex page rendering (Jinja/Django templates)          │
│     • Session management                                       │
│     • WebSocket connections (real-time features)               │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Long-Running Processes                                      │
│     • Celery workers (> 15 minutes)                            │
│     • Database migrations                                      │
│     • Large batch jobs                                         │
│     • Real-time data streaming                                 │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Stateful Applications                                       │
│     • User sessions in memory                                  │
│     • Caching layers (Redis on EC2)                            │
│     • File system dependencies                                 │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Consistent Traffic Patterns                                 │
│     • 24/7 availability required                               │
│     • Predictable baseline load                                │
│     • Reserved capacity cost savings                           │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Complex Dependencies                                        │
│     • Custom system libraries                                  │
│     • GPU requirements                                         │
│     • Large ML models (> 10 GB)                                │
│                                                                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  HYBRID APPROACH (RECOMMENDED FOR ANIHPJ):                     │
│                                                                 │
│  EC2: Main Django App + Database                               │
│   └─ Handles web requests, admin, complex business logic      │
│                                                                 │
│  Lambda: Event-Driven + APIs + Background Jobs                 │
│   ├─ API Gateway → Lambda (REST API for mobile apps)          │
│   ├─ S3 Trigger → Lambda (process uploaded files)             │
│   ├─ EventBridge → Lambda (scheduled cleanup tasks)           │
│   └─ SQS → Lambda (email notifications queue)                 │
│                                                                 │
│  Benefits:                                                     │
│   • Best of both worlds                                        │
│   • Cost optimization (pay-per-use for spiky workloads)       │
│   • Better scalability                                         │
│   • Reduced EC2 load                                           │
│   • Fault isolation                                            │
│                                                                 │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Cost Comparison Example:

Scenario: anihpj with 100,000 monthly active users

EC2 ONLY:
─────────
• t3.medium (2 vCPU, 4 GB): $30/month
• m5.large for peak hours: $70/month
• Total: ~$100/month (always running)

LAMBDA ONLY (API Backend):
──────────────────────────
• 5M API requests/month
• 300ms avg, 512 MB memory
• Request charges: $0.80
• Compute charges: $24.17
• Total: ~$25/month (pay-per-use)

HYBRID (RECOMMENDED):
────────────────────
• EC2 t3.small: $15/month (main app, reduced load)
• Lambda: $20/month (APIs, background tasks)
• Total: ~$35/month + better scalability

Winner: Hybrid approach saves 65% vs EC2-only!

📦 Typical Django Stack on AWS

A production-ready architecture for deploying Django applications using essential AWS services

🏗️ Complete Stack Architecture
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              TYPICAL DJANGO STACK ON AWS                       │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  1. EC2/ECS/Fargate                                           │
│     └─ Run Django application                                 │
│     └─ Gunicorn/uWSGI WSGI servers                           │
│     └─ Nginx for static file serving                         │
│                                                                │
│  2. RDS (PostgreSQL)                                          │
│     └─ Primary database                                       │
│     └─ Multi-AZ for high availability                        │
│     └─ Automated backups                                      │
│                                                                │
│  3. ElastiCache (Redis)                                       │
│     └─ Session store                                          │
│     └─ Application caching                                    │
│     └─ Celery broker for async tasks                         │
│                                                                │
│  4. S3                                                        │
│     └─ Static files (CSS/JS)                                 │
│     └─ Media uploads (user files, images)                    │
│     └─ Database backups                                       │
│                                                                │
│  5. CloudFront                                                │
│     └─ CDN for static/media files                           │
│     └─ Global content distribution                           │
│     └─ SSL/TLS termination                                   │
│                                                                │
│  6. ALB (Application Load Balancer)                           │
│     └─ Load balancing and SSL termination                    │
│     └─ Health checks and auto-scaling integration           │
│     └─ Path-based and host-based routing                     │
│                                                                │
│  7. Route 53                                                  │
│     └─ Domain and DNS management                             │
│     └─ Health checks and failover                           │
│     └─ Traffic routing policies                              │
│                                                                │
│  8. SQS                                                       │
│     └─ Celery task queue                                     │
│     └─ Asynchronous job processing                          │
│     └─ Decoupling microservices                             │
│                                                                │
│  9. CloudWatch                                                │
│     └─ Application logs and monitoring                        │
│     └─ Metrics and dashboards                                │
│     └─ Alarms and notifications                              │
│                                                                │
│  10. IAM                                                      │
│      └─ Access control and service permissions               │
│      └─ Role-based access for EC2/Lambda                     │
│      └─ Fine-grained S3 bucket policies                      │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
💡 Pro Tip: Start with EC2 + RDS + S3 for the MVP, then add ElastiCache, CloudFront, and other services as your application scales.

⚙️ Daily DevOps Tasks

Essential daily operations for maintaining AWS infrastructure and Django applications

📋 Daily Checklist
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                   DAILY DEVOPS TASKS                           │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  ☑ CloudWatch - Check logs and metrics                        │
│     • Review application error logs                           │
│     • Check CPU/Memory utilization                            │
│     • Monitor response times and latency                      │
│     • Verify alarm status                                     │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ EC2/ECS - Monitor instance health                          │
│     • Check instance status and health checks                 │
│     • Review auto-scaling events                              │
│     • Verify disk space usage                                 │
│     • Update security patches if needed                       │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ CodePipeline - Deploy code changes                         │
│     • Review pull requests                                    │
│     • Monitor CI/CD pipeline status                           │
│     • Verify deployment success                               │
│     • Rollback if issues detected                             │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ IAM - Manage user access                                   │
│     • Review access logs                                      │
│     • Update user permissions as needed                       │
│     • Rotate access keys (monthly)                            │
│     • Audit unused credentials                                │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ RDS - Database performance tuning                          │
│     • Check slow query logs                                   │
│     • Monitor connection pool usage                           │
│     • Review backup status                                    │
│     • Optimize indexes if needed                              │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ S3 - Manage backups and static files                       │
│     • Verify backup completion                                │
│     • Check storage costs                                     │
│     • Review lifecycle policies                               │
│     • Clear old temporary files                               │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ CloudFormation - Update infrastructure                     │
│     • Review stack drift detection                            │
│     • Apply infrastructure changes                            │
│     • Update stack parameters                                 │
│     • Document changes in version control                     │
│                                                                │
│  ☑ Systems Manager - Execute commands on servers              │
│     • Run maintenance scripts                                 │
│     • Update package repositories                             │
│     • Collect system inventory                                │
│     • Execute patch baselines                                 │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
⏰ Automation Tip: Many of these tasks can be automated using Lambda functions, CloudWatch Events, and Systems Manager Automation documents. Focus on automating repetitive checks first!

AWS Elastic Beanstalk

Category: Compute  |  Use Case: Managed Web Application Deployment  |  Pricing: No Additional Charge (Pay for AWS Resources)  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS Elastic Beanstalk Docs

Easy-to-use service for deploying and scaling web applications. Simply upload your Django code and Elastic Beanstalk automatically handles deployment, capacity provisioning, load balancing, and auto-scaling.

📋 Overview & Introduction

AWS Elastic Beanstalk is a Platform as a Service (PaaS) offering that simplifies deploying, managing, and scaling web applications. It abstracts away infrastructure management while still giving you full control when needed.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Quick Deployment: Deploy Django applications in minutes without infrastructure management
  • Automatic Scaling: Built-in auto-scaling based on your application's needs
  • Managed Updates: Automatic platform updates and patches
  • Full Control: Access to underlying resources (EC2, RDS, Load Balancers) when needed
  • Zero Additional Cost: Pay only for AWS resources (EC2, RDS, etc.), no Beanstalk fee
  • Multiple Environments: Easily manage dev, staging, and production environments
  • Integrated Monitoring: Built-in health monitoring and CloudWatch integration
💡 When to Use Elastic Beanstalk: Perfect for your anihpj Django job portal when you want fast deployment without managing servers, automatic scaling for traffic spikes during job postings, and easy environment management (dev/staging/production). Ideal for teams that want to focus on application code rather than infrastructure.
⚖️ Elastic Beanstalk vs. Other Compute Services
Service Control Level Management Best For anihpj Use Case
Elastic Beanstalk Medium (Managed PaaS) AWS manages infrastructure Web apps, APIs Quick Django deployment with auto-scaling
EC2 High (Full Control) You manage everything Custom configurations Custom server setup, WebSockets, background jobs
Lambda Low (Serverless) AWS manages all infrastructure Event-driven, short tasks Job notification triggers, image processing
Fargate Medium (Serverless containers) AWS manages servers Containerized microservices Docker-based Django deployment
🏗️ Elastic Beanstalk Architecture for Django
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                       AWS ELASTIC BEANSTALK ENVIRONMENT                 │
│                         (anihpj-jobportal-prod)                        │

│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Application

A logical collection of Elastic Beanstalk components (environments, versions, configurations).

eb init anihpj-jobportal --platform python-3.11
2. Environment

A version of your application running on AWS resources. Each environment has its own URL and configuration.

  • Web Server Environment: Handles HTTP requests (Django app)
  • Worker Environment: Processes background tasks from SQS
3. Platform

Combination of OS, runtime, web server, and application server. For anihpj: Python 3.11 on Amazon Linux 2023.

4. Configuration (.ebextensions)

YAML files to customize environment settings:

# .ebextensions/django.config
option_settings:
  aws:elasticbeanstalk:container:python:
    WSGIPath: "anihpj.wsgi:application"
  aws:autoscaling:asg:
    MinSize: 2
    MaxSize: 10

🚀 Getting Started with Elastic Beanstalk for Django

Step 1: Install EB CLI
pip install awsebcli
eb --version
Step 2: Initialize Application
cd /path/to/anihpj
eb init -p python-3.11 anihpj-jobportal --region us-east-1
Step 3: Configure Django Settings
# settings.py
import os

ALLOWED_HOSTS = ['.elasticbeanstalk.com', 'anihpj.com']

if 'RDS_HOSTNAME' in os.environ:
    DATABASES = {
        'default': {
            'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
            'NAME': os.environ['RDS_DB_NAME'],
            'USER': os.environ['RDS_USERNAME'],
            'PASSWORD': os.environ['RDS_PASSWORD'],
            'HOST': os.environ['RDS_HOSTNAME'],
            'PORT': os.environ['RDS_PORT'],
        }
    }
Step 4: Create Environment
eb create anihpj-prod \
    --instance-type t3.small \
    --scale 2 \
    --database \
    --database.engine postgres
Step 5: Deploy Application
eb deploy
eb open  # Opens in browser

🔑 Key Features & Components

1. Automatic Load Balancing

Distributes traffic across EC2 instances with health checks.

2. Auto Scaling

Automatically adjusts instance count based on CPU, memory, or request metrics.

3. Deployment Policies
Policy Downtime Speed Best For
All at Once Yes ⚡ Fastest Dev environments
Rolling No ⏱️ Medium Small apps
Immutable No 🐌 Slow Critical production
Blue-Green No ⏱️ Medium Zero-downtime
4. Managed Platform Updates

Automatic security patches and platform updates during maintenance windows.

5. Environment Health Monitoring

Real-time dashboard showing application health status (Green/Yellow/Red).

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 Key Point: Elastic Beanstalk is FREE. You only pay for underlying AWS resources (EC2, RDS, S3, Load Balancer).
🎯 Key Point

Elastic Beanstalk is FREE. You only pay for underlying AWS resources (EC2, RDS, S3, Load Balancer).

Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Resource Configuration Monthly Cost
EC2 Instances 2x t3.small $30
Load Balancer Application LB $20
RDS PostgreSQL db.t3.micro $15
S3 Storage 100GB media $2
Data Transfer 100GB out $10
Total ~$77/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Right-size instances: Start with t3.micro, scale as needed
  • Time-based scaling: Scale down during off-peak hours (nights/weekends)
  • Terminate dev environments: When not in use
  • Use S3 + CloudFront: For static files (cheaper than EC2 storage)
  • Reserved Instances: For predictable production workloads (save up to 72%)

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Auto Scaling Configuration
# .ebextensions/autoscaling.config
option_settings:
  aws:autoscaling:asg:
    MinSize: 2
    MaxSize: 10
  aws:autoscaling:trigger:
    MeasureName: CPUUtilization
    UpperThreshold: 75
    LowerThreshold: 25
Multi-AZ Deployment

Deploy across multiple availability zones for 99.95% uptime:

  • ✅ Instances distributed across 2-3 AZs
  • ✅ Multi-AZ RDS for database high availability
  • ✅ Load balancer automatically routes traffic
  • ✅ Automatic failover within 60-120 seconds

eb create anihpj-worker --tier worker
3. Blue-Green Deployments
eb clone anihpj-prod --clone_name anihpj-green
eb swap anihpj-prod --destination-name anihpj-green

💼 Common Use Cases

Use Case 1: Django Job Portal (anihpj)

Scenario: Deploy full-featured job posting platform with auto-scaling.

# Complete setup for anihpj
eb init anihpj-jobportal -p python-3.11
eb create anihpj-prod --instance-type t3.small --scale 2 --database

Use Case 2: Multi-Environment Workflow

Maintain dev, staging, and production environments:

eb create anihpj-dev --single --instance-type t3.micro
eb create anihpj-staging --scale 2
eb create anihpj-prod --scale 2 --database
Use Case 3: REST API Backend

Deploy Django REST Framework API for mobile apps with request-based scaling.

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj Django Deployment
Common Deployment Issues
  • 502 Bad Gateway: Check WSGI path, verify app is running on port 8000
  • Health Check Failures: Ensure /health/ endpoint returns HTTP 200
  • Static Files 404: Run collectstatic, configure proxy settings
  • Database Connection: Verify RDS security group allows EC2 access
  • Deployment Timeout: Check container_commands, migrations may be too slow

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

Essential EB CLI Commands
# Initialize application
eb init -p python-3.11 anihpj-jobportal

# Create environment
eb create anihpj-prod --instance-type t3.small --scale 2

# Deploy application
eb deploy
eb deploy --label v1.5.0 --message "Added search filters"

# Environment management
eb use anihpj-prod
eb status
eb health
eb open

# Scaling
eb scale 5
eb setenv MIN_INSTANCES=2 MAX_INSTANCES=10

# Configuration
eb config
eb setenv DEBUG=False SECRET_KEY=xyz
eb printenv

# Logs
eb logs
eb logs --stream
eb ssh

# Swap URLs (blue-green)
eb swap anihpj-prod --destination-name anihpj-staging

# Terminate
eb terminate anihpj-dev

🔗 Integration with AWS Services

Key AWS Service Integrations for anihpj
1. RDS (PostgreSQL Database)
# Auto-configured environment variables
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': os.environ.get('RDS_DB_NAME'),
        'USER': os.environ.get('RDS_USERNAME'),
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('RDS_PASSWORD'),
        'HOST': os.environ.get('RDS_HOSTNAME'),
        'PORT': os.environ.get('RDS_PORT', '5432'),
    }
}
2. S3 (Static/Media Files)
# settings.py - Django Storages
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-media'
AWS_S3_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_DEFAULT_ACL = 'public-read'
STATICFILES_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
DEFAULT_FILE_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
3. SES (Email Service)
# Email configuration
EMAIL_BACKEND = 'django_ses.SESBackend'
AWS_SES_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_SES_REGION_ENDPOINT = 'email.us-east-1.amazonaws.com'
DEFAULT_FROM_EMAIL = 'noreply@anihpj.com'

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

Automated Deployment Pipeline
GitHub Actions CI/CD for anihpj:
# .github/workflows/deploy.yml
name: Deploy to Elastic Beanstalk

on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Generate deployment package
      run: zip -r deploy.zip . -x '*.git*'
    
    - name: Deploy to EB
      uses: einaregilsson/beanstalk-deploy@v21
      with:
        aws_access_key: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        aws_secret_key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        application_name: anihpj-jobportal
        environment_name: anihpj-prod
        version_label: ${{ github.sha }}
        region: us-east-1
        deployment_package: deploy.zip

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001 (inherited from AWS services)
  • Encryption: At-rest (EBS, RDS, S3) and in-transit (TLS/SSL)
  • IAM Roles: Use instance profiles for secure AWS service access
  • VPC: Deploy in private subnets with NAT gateway
  • Monitoring: CloudWatch Logs, CloudTrail for audit trails
✅ anihpj Production Checklist:
  • ✅ HTTPS enforced with ACM certificate
  • ✅ Secrets in AWS Secrets Manager
  • ✅ Multi-AZ deployment (HA)
  • ✅ Automated backups (RDS 7-day retention)
  • ✅ CloudWatch monitoring + alarms
  • ✅ Security groups properly configured
  • ✅ IAM roles with least-privilege access
🎉 AWS Elastic Beanstalk Summary

Elastic Beanstalk is the fastest way to deploy your anihpj Django job portal to AWS. With zero additional cost, automatic scaling, and managed updates, you can focus on building features while AWS handles the infrastructure.

Perfect for: Django web apps, REST APIs, quick deployments, development teams focused on application code.

Cost: ~$70-150/month for production-ready setup with HA.

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Application Logical collection of Elastic Beanstalk components (environments, versions, configurations). For anihpj: "anihpj-jobportal"
Environment Collection of AWS resources running an application version. Examples: anihpj-dev, anihpj-staging, anihpj-prod
Environment Tier Web Server (HTTP traffic) or Worker (background jobs from SQS)
Platform Combination of OS, runtime, web server, and application server. E.g., "Python 3.11 running on 64bit Amazon Linux 2023"
Application Version Specific, labeled iteration of deployable code for an application. E.g., "v1.5.0-job-search-feature"
.ebextensions Directory containing YAML files to customize environment configuration and resources
.platform Directory for advanced platform customization using hooks and scripts
EB CLI Command-line interface for creating, managing, and deploying Beanstalk applications
Blue-Green Deployment Deployment strategy using two identical environments to enable zero-downtime updates
Immutable Deployment Deployment that launches new instances with new code before terminating old ones
Rolling Deployment Deployment that updates instances in batches to maintain availability
Saved Configuration Template for environment settings that can be reused across environments
Health Reporting Enhanced monitoring showing application health based on metrics and health checks
Managed Updates Automatic platform updates during maintenance windows
WSGI Web Server Gateway Interface - Standard interface for Python web applications. Django uses: anihpj.wsgi:application

⚔️ Elastic Beanstalk vs. EC2 vs. Lambda vs. Fargate

Detailed Service Comparison for anihpj Django Deployment
Feature Elastic Beanstalk EC2 Lambda Fargate
Management Level Managed PaaS Infrastructure (IaaS) Serverless (FaaS) Serverless Containers
Control ⭐⭐⭐ Medium ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Full ⭐ Limited ⭐⭐⭐ Medium
Setup Time ⚡ 5-10 minutes 🐌 30-60 minutes ⚡⚡ 2-5 minutes ⚡ 10-15 minutes
Scaling Automatic (CPU-based) Manual or Auto Scaling Group Automatic (instant) Automatic (container-based)
Pricing Model Free (pay for resources) Hourly instance charges Per-request + duration Per-second (vCPU + memory)
anihpj Cost 💰 $70-150/month 💰💰 $100-200/month 💰 $10-50/month 💰 $80-180/month
Load Balancing ✅ Built-in (auto-created) Manual setup required ✅ API Gateway ✅ ALB/NLB integration
Health Monitoring ✅ Enhanced built-in CloudWatch only ✅ CloudWatch Logs ✅ Container Insights
Deployment eb deploy (1 command) Custom scripts/tools SAM/Serverless/CDK ECS/Docker push
Multi-Environment ✅ Easy (dev/staging/prod) Manual setup ✅ Stages/Aliases ✅ ECS Services
Database Integration ✅ RDS auto-config Manual configuration ⚠️ Connection pooling issues Manual configuration
WebSockets ✅ Supported ✅ Full support ✅ API Gateway (limited) ✅ Full support
Long-Running Tasks ✅ Worker tier ✅ Unlimited ❌ 15 min max ✅ Unlimited
Custom Software ⚠️ Limited (.ebextensions) ✅ Full control ❌ Runtime only ✅ Docker images
Maintenance Effort ⭐ Low (AWS manages) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ High ⭐ Very Low ⭐⭐ Low-Medium
🎯 When to Choose Each Service for anihpj
Choose Elastic Beanstalk when:
  • ✅ You want fast deployment without managing infrastructure
  • ✅ You need automatic scaling for traffic spikes (job posting deadlines)
  • ✅ You want easy multi-environment management (dev/staging/prod)
  • ✅ Your team focuses on Django code, not DevOps
  • ✅ You need traditional web app architecture with persistent connections
Choose EC2 when:
  • ✅ You need full control over server configuration
  • ✅ You have custom software requirements (specific OS, system packages)
  • ✅ You need WebSocket connections for real-time job alerts
  • ✅ You want to run background workers alongside web servers
  • ✅ Cost optimization through Reserved Instances for predictable load
Choose Lambda when:
  • ✅ Building event-driven features (job notification triggers)
  • ✅ Image processing for resume uploads
  • ✅ Scheduled tasks (daily job expiration checks)
  • ✅ API endpoints with sporadic traffic
  • ✅ You want to pay only for actual execution time
Choose Fargate when:
  • ✅ You prefer Docker-based deployments
  • ✅ You need microservices architecture
  • ✅ You want serverless but with containers
  • ✅ You need precise resource control (vCPU/memory)
  • ✅ You have existing Docker workflows
💡 Hybrid Approach for anihpj (Recommended)
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                   anihpj Hybrid Architecture                  │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                               │
│  🌐 Elastic Beanstalk (Primary Web Application)              │
│     ├─ Django job portal web interface                       │
│     ├─ User authentication & job browsing                    │
│     ├─ Application submission forms                          │
│     └─ Auto-scaling: 2-10 instances                          │
│                                                               │
│  ⚡ Lambda Functions (Event-Driven Tasks)                     │
│     ├─ Email notifications (new job alerts)                  │
│     ├─ Resume file processing & virus scanning               │
│     ├─ Daily job expiration cleanup                          │
│     └─ Webhook handlers for third-party integrations         │
│                                                               │
│  💾 RDS PostgreSQL (Shared Database)                          │
│     └─ Central data store for both Beanstalk & Lambda        │
│                                                               │
│  📦 S3 + CloudFront                                           │
│     └─ Static files & media (resumes, company logos)         │
│                                                               │

│  💰 Estimated Cost: $120-180/month                            │
