🎓 Final Recommendation for anihpj:

Start with Elastic Beanstalk for the main Django application. It provides the best balance of simplicity, features, and cost for a job portal. As your application grows, add Lambda functions for specific event-driven tasks and consider EC2 for specialized workloads that need custom configuration.

Migration Path: Beanstalk (MVP) → Beanstalk + Lambda (Scale) → Beanstalk + Lambda + EC2 Workers (Enterprise)

AWS Fargate

Category: Compute  |  Use Case: Serverless Container Orchestration  |  Pricing: Per-Second vCPU and Memory  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS Fargate Docs

Serverless compute engine for containers that works with Amazon ECS and EKS. Deploy and manage containers without managing servers or clusters, paying only for the resources your containerized applications use.

📋 Overview & Introduction

AWS Fargate is a serverless compute engine for containers that removes the need to provision and manage servers. You define your application's requirements (CPU, memory, networking) and Fargate launches and scales the compute, allowing you to focus on building applications rather than managing infrastructure.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Serverless: No servers to provision, patch, or scale
  • Container-Native: Deploy Docker containers with full isolation
  • Pay-per-Use: Pay only for vCPU and memory resources consumed per second
  • Scalable: Automatically scales with application demand
  • Secure: Task-level isolation with AWS IAM and VPC networking
  • Integrated: Works seamlessly with ECS and EKS
  • Flexible: Support for various compute configurations
💡 When to Use Fargate: Perfect for your anihpj Django job portal when you want containerized deployments without managing EC2 instances, microservices architecture, or batch processing jobs. Ideal for teams familiar with Docker who want the benefits of containers without infrastructure overhead.
⚖️ Fargate vs. Other Compute Services
Service Management Best For anihpj Use Case
Fargate Serverless containers Containerized apps, microservices Docker-based Django with auto-scaling
ECS on EC2 Container orchestration on EC2 Custom instance requirements Cost optimization with Reserved Instances
EKS Managed Kubernetes Complex orchestration needs Advanced microservices with Kubernetes
Lambda Serverless functions Event-driven, short tasks Job notification triggers
EC2 Full server control Custom configurations Traditional deployment with full access
🏗️ Fargate Architecture for Django
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│  │                  (anihpj-fargate-alb)                            │  │

│                           │                 │                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────▼────┐  ┌─────────▼──────────────────────┐  │

│  │                             │  │                            │  │

│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │                    ECS Service Auto Scaling                       │  │
│  │  • Desired: 2  • Min: 1  • Max: 10                               │  │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                    │
                        ┌───────────▼───────────────┐
                        │   RDS PostgreSQL          │
                        │   (anihpj-jobportal-db)   │
                        └───────────────────────────┘

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Task Definition

Blueprint for your application that specifies containers, CPU, memory, networking, and IAM roles. Like a Dockerfile configuration but for AWS.

{
  "family": "anihpj-django-task",
  "networkMode": "awsvpc",
  "requiresCompatibilities": ["FARGATE"],
  "cpu": "512",
  "memory": "1024",
  "containerDefinitions": [{
    "name": "anihpj-web",
    "image": "123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest",
    "portMappings": [{"containerPort": 8000, "protocol": "tcp"}],
    "environment": [
      {"name": "DEBUG", "value": "False"},
      {"name": "DATABASE_URL", "value": "postgresql://..."}
    ]
  }]
}
2. Service

Manages and maintains the desired number of task instances. Ensures tasks are running and integrates with load balancers.

3. Cluster

Logical grouping of tasks or services. With Fargate, you don't manage the underlying infrastructure.

4. Task vs Task Definition
  • Task Definition: Template (blueprint)
  • Task: Running instance of a task definition
  • Think: Class (Task Definition) vs Object (Task)

🚀 Getting Started with Fargate for Django

Step 1: Create Dockerfile for anihpj
# Dockerfile
FROM python:3.11-slim

WORKDIR /app

# Install dependencies
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt
RUN pip install gunicorn psycopg2-binary

# Copy application
COPY . .

# Collect static files
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Expose port
EXPOSE 8000

# Run application
CMD ["gunicorn", "anihpj.wsgi:application", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8000", "--workers", "3"]
Step 2: Build and Push to ECR
# Authenticate Docker to ECR
aws ecr get-login-password --region us-east-1 | docker login --username AWS --password-stdin 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com

# Create ECR repository
aws ecr create-repository --repository-name anihpj --region us-east-1

# Build Docker image
docker build -t anihpj:latest .

# Tag image
docker tag anihpj:latest 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest

# Push to ECR
docker push 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest
Step 3: Create Task Definition
# Create task-definition.json
aws ecs register-task-definition --cli-input-json file://task-definition.json
Step 4: Create ECS Cluster
aws ecs create-cluster --cluster-name anihpj-cluster --region us-east-1
Step 5: Create Service
aws ecs create-service \
    --cluster anihpj-cluster \
    --service-name anihpj-service \
    --task-definition anihpj-django-task \
    --desired-count 2 \
    --launch-type FARGATE \
    --network-configuration "awsvpcConfiguration={subnets=[subnet-12345],securityGroups=[sg-12345],assignPublicIp=ENABLED}" \
    --load-balancers "targetGroupArn=arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:...,containerName=anihpj-web,containerPort=8000"

🔑 Key Features & Components

1. Serverless Infrastructure

No EC2 instances to manage. AWS handles provisioning, scaling, and maintenance automatically.

2. Task-Level Isolation

Each task runs in its own isolated environment with dedicated kernel, CPU, memory, and network resources.

3. Right-Sizing Options
CPU (vCPU) Memory Options (GB) anihpj Recommendation
0.25 0.5, 1, 2 Development/Testing
0.5 1, 2, 3, 4 ✅ Small Production (Recommended)
1 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8 Medium Production
2 4-16 GB Large Production
4 8-30 GB High Traffic
4. AWS VPC Networking

Tasks run within your VPC with full control over security groups, subnets, and network ACLs.

5. Integrated Monitoring

CloudWatch Container Insights for metrics, logs, and traces. X-Ray for distributed tracing.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 Fargate Pricing Model:

Pay only for vCPU and memory resources used per second (1-minute minimum). No charges for idle infrastructure.

Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Resource Configuration Monthly Cost
Fargate Tasks 2x (0.5 vCPU, 1GB) running 24/7 $35
Application Load Balancer Standard ALB $20
RDS PostgreSQL db.t3.micro $15
ECR Storage 5GB Docker images $0.50
Data Transfer 100GB out $10
Total ~$80/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Right-size tasks: Start small (0.25 vCPU) and scale up based on metrics
  • Use Spot capacity: Save up to 70% for fault-tolerant workloads
  • Scale to zero: For dev/test environments, scale down when not in use
  • Optimize Docker images: Smaller images = faster startup = lower costs
  • Use Savings Plans: Commit to consistent usage for 20-50% savings
  • Consolidate containers: Run multiple related containers in one task

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Auto Scaling Configuration
# Register scalable target
aws application-autoscaling register-scalable-target \
    --service-namespace ecs \
    --resource-id service/anihpj-cluster/anihpj-service \
    --scalable-dimension ecs:service:DesiredCount \
    --min-capacity 1 \
    --max-capacity 10

# Create CPU-based scaling policy
aws application-autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --policy-name anihpj-cpu-scaling \
    --service-namespace ecs \
    --resource-id service/anihpj-cluster/anihpj-service \
    --scalable-dimension ecs:service:DesiredCount \
    --policy-type TargetTrackingScaling \
    --target-tracking-scaling-policy-configuration file://scaling-policy.json
Multi-AZ Deployment

Best practices for high availability:

  • ✅ Deploy tasks across 2-3 availability zones
  • ✅ Use Application Load Balancer for health checks
  • ✅ Configure task placement strategies
  • ✅ Set up automatic task recovery
  • ✅ Multi-AZ RDS for database redundancy

🎓 Advanced Topics

1. Fargate Spot

Run fault-tolerant tasks at up to 70% discount:

{
  "capacityProviderStrategy": [
    {
      "capacityProvider": "FARGATE_SPOT",
      "weight": 4,
      "base": 0
    },
    {
      "capacityProvider": "FARGATE",
      "weight": 1,
      "base": 2
    }
  ]
}
2. Secrets Management

Store sensitive data securely:

"secrets": [
  {
    "name": "DATABASE_PASSWORD",
    "valueFrom": "arn:aws:secretsmanager:us-east-1:123456789012:secret:anihpj-db-password"
  },
  {
    "name": "SECRET_KEY",
    "valueFrom": "arn:aws:secretsmanager:us-east-1:123456789012:secret:anihpj-django-secret"
  }
]
3. EFS Integration for Persistent Storage
"volumes": [{
  "name": "anihpj-media",
  "efsVolumeConfiguration": {
    "fileSystemId": "fs-12345678",
    "transitEncryption": "ENABLED"
  }
}]
4. CI/CD with GitHub Actions
# .github/workflows/deploy-fargate.yml
name: Deploy to Fargate
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Configure AWS credentials
        uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v2
        with:
          aws-access-key-id: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
          aws-secret-access-key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
          aws-region: us-east-1
      
      - name: Login to Amazon ECR
        id: login-ecr
        uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v1
      
      - name: Build and push Docker image
        env:
          ECR_REGISTRY: ${{ steps.login-ecr.outputs.registry }}
          ECR_REPOSITORY: anihpj
          IMAGE_TAG: ${{ github.sha }}
        run: |
          docker build -t $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG .
          docker push $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG
      
      - name: Update ECS service
        run: |
          aws ecs update-service \
            --cluster anihpj-cluster \
            --service anihpj-service \
            --force-new-deployment

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj Fargate Deployment
Common Deployment Issues
  • Task Fails to Start: Check CloudWatch logs, verify Docker image exists in ECR
  • Out of Memory: Increase memory allocation in task definition
  • Network Timeout: Verify security groups allow outbound traffic, check NAT gateway
  • Cannot Pull Image: Verify IAM role has ECR permissions
  • Health Check Failing: Ensure container exposes correct port and responds to health checks
Frequently Asked Questions
  • Q: Can I SSH into Fargate tasks?
    A: No, but you can use ECS Exec for debugging
  • Q: How do I persist data?
    A: Use EFS volumes or external databases like RDS
  • Q: What's the cold start time?
    A: Typically 30-60 seconds for task startup
  • Q: Can I use GPU?
    A: Yes, Fargate supports GPU tasks for ML workloads
  • Q: How do I debug issues?
    A: Use CloudWatch Logs, Container Insights, and AWS X-Ray

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

Essential ECS/Fargate CLI Commands
# Cluster Management
aws ecs create-cluster --cluster-name anihpj-cluster
aws ecs list-clusters
aws ecs describe-clusters --clusters anihpj-cluster
aws ecs delete-cluster --cluster anihpj-cluster

# Task Definitions
aws ecs register-task-definition --cli-input-json file://task-def.json
aws ecs list-task-definitions
aws ecs describe-task-definition --task-definition anihpj-django-task
aws ecs deregister-task-definition --task-definition anihpj-django-task:1

# Services
aws ecs create-service --cli-input-json file://service.json
aws ecs list-services --cluster anihpj-cluster
aws ecs describe-services --cluster anihpj-cluster --services anihpj-service
aws ecs update-service --cluster anihpj-cluster --service anihpj-service --force-new-deployment
aws ecs delete-service --cluster anihpj-cluster --service anihpj-service

# Tasks
aws ecs list-tasks --cluster anihpj-cluster
aws ecs describe-tasks --cluster anihpj-cluster --tasks task-id
aws ecs run-task --cluster anihpj-cluster --task-definition anihpj-django-task --launch-type FARGATE
aws ecs stop-task --cluster anihpj-cluster --task task-id

# Logs
aws logs tail /ecs/anihpj-django-task --follow
aws logs get-log-events --log-group-name /ecs/anihpj-django-task --log-stream-name ecs/anihpj-web/task-id

# Django settings.py for Fargate
import os

DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': os.environ.get('DB_NAME', 'anihpj'),
        'USER': os.environ.get('DB_USER', 'postgres'),
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD'),  # From Secrets Manager
        'HOST': os.environ.get('DB_HOST'),
        'PORT': os.environ.get('DB_PORT', '5432'),
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,
    }
}
2. ECR (Container Registry)
# Build and push workflow
aws ecr create-repository --repository-name anihpj
$(aws ecr get-login --no-include-email)
docker build -t anihpj:latest .
docker tag anihpj:latest 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest
docker push 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest

# Task IAM role grants SES permissions
EMAIL_BACKEND = 'django_ses.SESBackend'

DEFAULT_FROM_EMAIL = 'noreply@anihpj.com'

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

Complete GitHub Actions Workflow
# .github/workflows/deploy-to-fargate.yml
name: Deploy anihpj to AWS Fargate

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

env:
  AWS_REGION: us-east-1
  ECR_REPOSITORY: anihpj
  ECS_CLUSTER: anihpj-cluster
  ECS_SERVICE: anihpj-service
  ECS_TASK_DEFINITION: anihpj-django-task

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - name: Checkout code
      uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Configure AWS credentials
      uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v2
      with:
        aws-access-key-id: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        aws-secret-access-key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        aws-region: ${{ env.AWS_REGION }}
    
    - name: Login to Amazon ECR
      id: login-ecr
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v1
    
    - name: Build, tag, and push image to Amazon ECR
      id: build-image
      env:
        ECR_REGISTRY: ${{ steps.login-ecr.outputs.registry }}
        IMAGE_TAG: ${{ github.sha }}
      run: |
        docker build -t $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG .
        docker push $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG
        echo "image=$ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
    
    - name: Download task definition
      run: |
        aws ecs describe-task-definition \
          --task-definition ${{ env.ECS_TASK_DEFINITION }} \
          --query taskDefinition > task-definition.json
    
    - name: Fill in the new image ID in the Amazon ECS task definition
      id: task-def
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecs-render-task-definition@v1
      with:
        task-definition: task-definition.json
        container-name: anihpj-web
        image: ${{ steps.build-image.outputs.image }}
    
    - name: Deploy Amazon ECS task definition
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecs-deploy-task-definition@v1
      with:
        task-definition: ${{ steps.task-def.outputs.task-definition }}
        service: ${{ env.ECS_SERVICE }}
        cluster: ${{ env.ECS_CLUSTER }}
        wait-for-service-stability: true

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001, FedRAMP
  • Task Isolation: Dedicated kernel runtime per task
  • Encryption: At-rest (EBS volumes) and in-transit (TLS)
  • IAM Integration: Fine-grained task-level permissions
  • VPC Security: Private networking with security groups
✅ anihpj Fargate Production Checklist:
  • ✅ Tasks in private subnets with NAT gateway
  • ✅ Secrets in AWS Secrets Manager
  • ✅ Multi-AZ task deployment
  • ✅ CloudWatch Container Insights enabled
  • ✅ ALB with HTTPS and ACM certificate
  • ✅ Task IAM roles with least privilege
  • ✅ Auto Scaling configured (min 2, max 10)
  • ✅ RDS automated backups enabled
  • ✅ Docker image vulnerability scanning
  • ✅ CI/CD pipeline for automated deployments

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Task Definition Blueprint specifying containers, CPU, memory, and networking for your application
Task Running instance of a task definition (similar to EC2 instance)
Service Manages desired number of task instances and integrates with load balancers
Cluster Logical grouping of tasks and services
ECR Elastic Container Registry - AWS Docker image repository
ECS Elastic Container Service - Container orchestration service
awsvpc Network mode giving each task an elastic network interface (ENI)
Launch Type FARGATE (serverless) or EC2 (manage instances)
Capacity Provider Strategy for task placement (FARGATE, FARGATE_SPOT)
Task Role IAM role for applications running in task containers
Execution Role IAM role for ECS agent (pull images, send logs)
Container Insights CloudWatch monitoring for containerized applications
Fargate Spot Run tasks on spare Fargate capacity at up to 70% discount

🎯 When to Choose Fargate for anihpj
Choose Fargate when:
  • ✅ You want containerized Django without managing servers
  • ✅ You need microservices architecture (API + Workers + Services)
  • ✅ You prefer Docker-based deployments
  • ✅ You want pay-per-use pricing without idle costs
  • ✅ You need task-level security isolation
  • ✅ You want to avoid EC2 instance management overhead

💾 Storage Services

AWS offers various storage solutions for different use cases, from object storage to block storage and file systems.

Amazon S3 (Simple Storage Service)

Category: Storage  |  Use Case: Object Storage for Static Files, Media, Backups  |  Pricing: Pay-per-GB Stored + Data Transfer  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS S3 Docs

Amazon S3 is an object storage service offering industry-leading scalability, data availability, security, and performance. Perfect for storing Django static files, user-uploaded media (resumes, company logos), backups, and application data.

📋 Overview & Introduction

Amazon S3 provides object storage through a web services interface. You can store and retrieve any amount of data at any time from anywhere on the web. It's designed for 99.999999999% (11 9's) durability and stores data for millions of applications.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Durability: 99.999999999% (11 9's) object durability
  • Scalability: Store unlimited data without capacity planning
  • Availability: 99.99% availability SLA for Standard tier
  • Security: Encryption at rest and in transit, IAM policies, bucket policies
  • Performance: Automatically scales to high request rates
  • Cost-Effective: Multiple storage classes for cost optimization
  • Integration: Works seamlessly with Django, CloudFront, Lambda
💡 Perfect for anihpj: Store Django static files (CSS, JS), user-uploaded resumes, company logos, job posting attachments, database backups, and application logs. S3 is the foundation for scalable file storage in your job portal.
⚖️ S3 vs. Other Storage Services
Service Type Best For anihpj Use Case
S3 Object Storage Static files, media, backups Resumes, logos, static assets
EBS Block Storage EC2 instance volumes EC2 root volume, databases
EFS File Storage Shared file systems Shared media across multiple servers
Glacier Archive Storage Long-term archival Old job posting archives, compliance

│  │  Lifecycle Policy: Delete after 180 days (auto-cleanup)   │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                   │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │  S3 Bucket: anihpj-backups                                 │  │
│  │  ├─ database/                                              │  │
│  │  │  └─ postgres_backup_2025-11-03.sql.gz                   │  │
│  │  └─ application/                                           │  │
│  │     └─ media_backup_weekly.tar.gz                          │  │
│  │                                                             │  │
│  │  Storage Class: S3 Standard-IA (Infrequent Access)        │  │
│  │  Lifecycle: Transition to Glacier after 90 days            │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                   │
│  💰 Estimated Cost: $5-15/month (100GB storage + transfer)       │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                 │
                    ┌────────────▼────────────┐
                    │   Django Application    │
                    │   (django-storages)     │
                    └─────────────────────────┘

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Buckets

Containers for storing objects. Bucket names must be globally unique across all AWS accounts.

# Create bucket for anihpj
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-static --region us-east-1
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-media --region us-east-1
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-backups --region us-east-1
2. Objects

Files stored in S3. Each object consists of data, metadata, and a unique key (filename).

  • Key: Object name/path (e.g., resumes/user_123/resume.pdf)
  • Value: The actual file data (up to 5TB per object)
  • Metadata: Key-value pairs describing the object
  • Version ID: If versioning is enabled
3. Storage Classes
Class Use Case Availability Cost
Standard Frequently accessed 99.99% $$
Standard-IA Infrequent access 99.9% $
One Zone-IA Non-critical, infrequent 99.5% $
Glacier Archive (minutes-hours) 99.99% ¢
Glacier Deep Long-term archive 99.99% ¢
4. Versioning

Keep multiple variants of an object. Protects from accidental deletions and overwrites.

5. Access Control
  • IAM Policies: User/role-based permissions
  • Bucket Policies: Resource-based permissions
  • ACLs: Legacy access control lists
  • Pre-signed URLs: Temporary access to private objects

🚀 Getting Started with S3 for Django

Step 1: Install Required Packages
# Install django-storages and boto3
pip install django-storages boto3

# Add to requirements.txt
echo "django-storages==1.14.2" >> requirements.txt
echo "boto3==1.34.18" >> requirements.txt
Step 2: Configure Django Settings
# anihpj/settings.py
import os

# Add to INSTALLED_APPS
INSTALLED_APPS = [
    # ... other apps
    'storages',
]

# AWS S3 Configuration
AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID = os.environ.get('AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID')
AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY = os.environ.get('AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY')
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-media'
AWS_S3_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = f'{AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME}.s3.amazonaws.com'

# Static files (CSS, JavaScript, Images)
STATICFILES_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'

# Media files (User uploads)
DEFAULT_FILE_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'

# Optional: Use CloudFront CDN
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'

# S3 Settings
AWS_S3_FILE_OVERWRITE = False
AWS_DEFAULT_ACL = None
AWS_S3_VERIFY = True
Step 3: Create S3 Buckets
# Create buckets
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-static
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-media
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-backups

# Enable versioning on media bucket
aws s3api put-bucket-versioning \
    --bucket anihpj-media \
    --versioning-configuration Status=Enabled

# Enable server-side encryption
aws s3api put-bucket-encryption \
    --bucket anihpj-media \
    --server-side-encryption-configuration '{
        "Rules": [{
            "ApplyServerSideEncryptionByDefault": {
                "SSEAlgorithm": "AES256"
            }
        }]
    }'
Step 4: Set Bucket Policy
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "PublicReadGetObject",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Principal": "*",
      "Action": "s3:GetObject",
      "Resource": "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-static/*"
    },
    {
      "Sid": "DjangoAppUpload",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Principal": {
        "AWS": "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:user/anihpj-app"
      },
      "Action": [
        "s3:PutObject",
        "s3:GetObject",
        "s3:DeleteObject"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-media/*"
    }
  ]
}
Step 5: Use S3 in Django Models
# jobpost/models.py
from django.db import models

class JobPost(models.Model):
    title = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    company_logo = models.ImageField(
        upload_to='company-logos/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Auto-uploads to S3: s3://anihpj-media/company-logos/
    
    job_description_pdf = models.FileField(
        upload_to='job-attachments/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Auto-uploads to S3
    
    created_at = models.DateTimeField(auto_now_add=True)

class UserProfile(models.Model):
    user = models.OneToOneField(User, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to='resumes/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Stored in: s3://anihpj-media/resumes/resume_xyz.pdf

🔑 Key Features & Capabilities

1. Lifecycle Management

Automatically transition objects between storage classes or delete them.

{
  "Rules": [
    {
      "Id": "ArchiveOldResumes",
      "Status": "Enabled",
      "Filter": {"Prefix": "resumes/"},
      "Transitions": [
        {
          "Days": 90,
          "StorageClass": "STANDARD_IA"
        },
        {
          "Days": 365,
          "StorageClass": "GLACIER"
        }
      ]
    },
    {
      "Id": "DeleteTempFiles",
      "Status": "Enabled",
      "Filter": {"Prefix": "temp/"},
      "Expiration": {"Days": 7}
    }
  ]
}
2. Cross-Region Replication

Automatically replicate objects across AWS regions for disaster recovery.

3. Event Notifications

Trigger Lambda functions, SQS queues, or SNS topics when objects are created/deleted.

# Lambda function triggered on resume upload
import boto3

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Get bucket and key from S3 event
    bucket = event['Records'][0]['s3']['bucket']['name']
    key = event['Records'][0]['s3']['object']['key']
    
    # Process uploaded resume (virus scan, format validation)
    print(f"New resume uploaded: s3://{bucket}/{key}")
    
    # Send notification to recruiter
    # ...
4. Pre-signed URLs

Generate temporary URLs for secure access to private objects.

# Django view to generate download link
import boto3
from datetime import timedelta

def generate_resume_download(request, resume_id):
    s3_client = boto3.client('s3')
    
    # Generate pre-signed URL (valid for 1 hour)
    url = s3_client.generate_presigned_url(
        'get_object',
        Params={
            'Bucket': 'anihpj-media',
            'Key': f'resumes/{resume_id}.pdf'
        },
        ExpiresIn=3600  # 1 hour
    )
    
    return JsonResponse({'download_url': url})
5. Transfer Acceleration

Use CloudFront edge locations to speed up uploads by up to 50-500%.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 S3 Pricing Components:
  • Storage: $0.023/GB/month (Standard, first 50TB)
  • Requests: $0.0004 per 1,000 PUT/POST, $0.0004 per 10,000 GET
  • Data Transfer: $0.09/GB out to internet (first 10TB)
  • Storage Classes: Standard-IA 50% cheaper, Glacier 90% cheaper
Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Component Usage Monthly Cost
Storage (Standard) 50GB static files + media $1.15
Storage (Standard-IA) 100GB backups $1.25
PUT/POST Requests 10,000 uploads/month $0.05
GET Requests 100,000 downloads/month $0.04
Data Transfer Out 20GB/month $1.80
CloudFront CDN 50GB transfer $4.25
Total ~$8.50/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Use CloudFront: Reduces S3 data transfer costs by 70%
  • Lifecycle policies: Auto-move old files to cheaper storage
  • Intelligent-Tiering: Auto-optimize based on access patterns
  • Delete unused files: Remove temp files, old backups
  • Compress files: Gzip CSS/JS before uploading
  • Right-size images: Don't store 10MB logos when 100KB works

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Automatic Scaling
  • ✅ Scales automatically to handle any request rate
  • ✅ Supports 3,500 PUT/POST and 5,500 GET requests per second per prefix
  • ✅ No capacity planning required
  • ✅ Partition keys (prefixes) for higher throughput
Durability & Availability
  • 99.999999999% durability: Data replicated across 3+ AZs
  • 99.99% availability: Designed for Standard class
  • Cross-Region Replication: For disaster recovery
  • Versioning: Protection against accidental deletion

🎓 Advanced Topics

1. S3 + CloudFront CDN

Serve static files from edge locations for faster delivery.

# Django settings with CloudFront
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'

# CloudFront distribution settings
# - Origin: anihpj-static.s3.amazonaws.com
# - Cache behavior: Cache based on query strings
# - TTL: 1 year for static, 1 hour for media
# - SSL Certificate: ACM certificate
2. Multipart Upload

Upload large files (>100MB) in parts for better performance.

import boto3
from boto3.s3.transfer import TransferConfig

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')

# Configure multipart upload (5MB chunks)
config = TransferConfig(
    multipart_threshold=1024 * 25,  # 25MB
    max_concurrency=10,
    multipart_chunksize=1024 * 25
)

# Upload large file
s3_client.upload_file(
    'large_video.mp4',
    'anihpj-media',
    'videos/large_video.mp4',
    Config=config
)
3. Server-Side Encryption
  • SSE-S3: AWS-managed keys (AES-256)
  • SSE-KMS: AWS KMS-managed keys (audit trail)
  • SSE-C: Customer-provided keys
4. Static Website Hosting
# Enable static website hosting
aws s3 website s3://anihpj-static \
    --index-document index.html \
    --error-document error.html

# Website endpoint: http://anihpj-static.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com

✨ Best Practices

💼 Common Use Cases

Use Case 1: Django Static Files

Scenario: Serve CSS, JavaScript, and images for anihpj from S3 + CloudFront.

# Collect static files to S3
python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Files are automatically uploaded to:
# s3://anihpj-static/static/css/
# s3://anihpj-static/static/js/
# s3://anihpj-static/static/images/
Use Case 2: User-Uploaded Files

Store resumes, company logos, and job attachments with automatic S3 upload.

# View for file upload
from django.core.files.storage import default_storage

def upload_resume(request):
    if request.method == 'POST':
        resume_file = request.FILES['resume']
        
        # Automatically uploads to S3
        file_path = default_storage.save(
            f'resumes/{request.user.id}/{resume_file.name}',
            resume_file
        )
        
        # Get S3 URL
        file_url = default_storage.url(file_path)
        # Returns: https://anihpj-media.s3.amazonaws.com/resumes/123/resume.pdf
Use Case 3: Database & Application Backups
# Automated backup script
#!/bin/bash
DATE=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)

# Backup PostgreSQL database
pg_dump anihpj_db | gzip > /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz

# Upload to S3
aws s3 cp /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz s3://anihpj-backups/database/

# Cleanup local file
rm /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj S3 Issues
Common Issues
  • 403 Forbidden: Check IAM permissions, bucket policy, and CORS configuration
  • Slow uploads: Use Transfer Acceleration or multipart uploads
  • Files not appearing: Verify bucket name, region, and AWS credentials
  • CORS errors: Configure CORS policy on S3 bucket
  • High costs: Review data transfer, implement lifecycle policies
Frequently Asked Questions
  • Q: What's the max file size?
    A: 5TB per object (use multipart upload for >5GB)
  • Q: Can I use custom domain?
    A: Yes, via CloudFront with Route 53
  • Q: How secure is S3?
    A: Very secure with encryption, IAM, VPC endpoints
  • Q: Can I host entire Django app?
    A: Only static files; use EC2/Fargate/Beanstalk for Django app
  • Q: How to prevent accidental deletion?
    A: Enable versioning + MFA Delete

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

Essential S3 CLI Commands
# Bucket Operations
aws s3 mb s3://bucket-name                    # Create bucket
aws s3 ls                                     # List all buckets
aws s3 ls s3://bucket-name                    # List objects in bucket
aws s3 rb s3://bucket-name --force            # Delete bucket and contents

# File Operations
aws s3 cp file.txt s3://bucket/path/          # Upload file
aws s3 cp s3://bucket/path/file.txt .         # Download file
aws s3 sync ./local s3://bucket/path/         # Sync directory
aws s3 rm s3://bucket/path/file.txt           # Delete file
aws s3 mv s3://bucket/old.txt s3://bucket/new.txt  # Move/rename

# Recursive Operations
aws s3 cp ./static s3://bucket/static/ --recursive
aws s3 rm s3://bucket/temp/ --recursive

# Pre-signed URLs
aws s3 presign s3://bucket/file.pdf --expires-in 3600

# Bucket Configuration
aws s3api get-bucket-versioning --bucket bucket-name
aws s3api put-bucket-versioning --bucket bucket-name \
    --versioning-configuration Status=Enabled

# Lifecycle Rules
aws s3api put-bucket-lifecycle-configuration \
    --bucket bucket-name \
    --lifecycle-configuration file://lifecycle.json

🔗 Integration with AWS Services

Key AWS Service Integrations for anihpj
1. CloudFront (CDN)
# Django settings with CloudFront
AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/static/'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/media/'

# Benefits:
# - 10x faster content delivery
# - 70% reduction in S3 costs
# - SSL/TLS encryption
# - DDoS protection
2. Lambda (Serverless Processing)
# Lambda function for image resizing
import boto3
from PIL import Image
import io

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    bucket = event['Records'][0]['s3']['bucket']['name']
    key = event['Records'][0]['s3']['object']['key']
    
    # Download original image
    response = s3_client.get_object(Bucket=bucket, Key=key)
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(response['Body'].read()))
    
    # Resize to thumbnail
    img.thumbnail((200, 200))
    
    # Save back to S3
    buffer = io.BytesIO()
    img.save(buffer, 'JPEG')
    buffer.seek(0)
    
    thumb_key = key.replace('logos/', 'logos/thumbnails/')
    s3_client.put_object(
        Bucket=bucket,
        Key=thumb_key,
        Body=buffer,
        ContentType='image/jpeg'
    )
3. RDS (Database Backups)
# Automated RDS backup to S3
aws rds create-db-snapshot \
    --db-instance-identifier anihpj-db \
    --db-snapshot-identifier anihpj-snapshot-$(date +%Y%m%d)

# Export snapshot to S3
aws rds start-export-task \
    --export-task-identifier anihpj-export \
    --source-arn arn:aws:rds:us-east-1:123456789012:snapshot:anihpj-snapshot \
    --s3-bucket-name anihpj-backups \
    --iam-role-arn arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/rds-s3-export

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

GitHub Actions Workflow for S3 Deployment
# .github/workflows/deploy-static-to-s3.yml
name: Deploy Static Files to S3

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Set up Python
      uses: actions/setup-python@v4
      with:
        python-version: '3.11'
    
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: |
        pip install -r requirements.txt
    
    - name: Collect static files
      run: |
        python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
      env:
        AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME: anihpj-static
    
    - name: Invalidate CloudFront cache
      run: |
        aws cloudfront create-invalidation \
          --distribution-id E1234ABCD \
          --paths "/*"
      env:
        AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC 1/2/3, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001, FedRAMP
  • Encryption: Server-side (SSE) and client-side encryption
  • Access Logging: Track all S3 API requests
  • Object Lock: WORM (Write Once Read Many) compliance
  • Macie: Discover and protect sensitive data (PII)
✅ anihpj S3 Production Checklist:
  • ✅ Enable encryption at rest (SSE-S3/KMS)
  • ✅ Enable versioning on critical buckets
  • ✅ Block public access unless required
  • ✅ Configure CORS for web uploads
  • ✅ Set up lifecycle policies for cost savings
  • ✅ Enable access logging
  • ✅ Use IAM roles instead of access keys
  • ✅ Configure CloudFront for static files
  • ✅ Implement backup strategy (versioning + replication)
  • ✅ Monitor with CloudWatch metrics

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Bucket Container for objects stored in S3 (like a top-level folder)
Object File stored in S3, consisting of data, metadata, and key
Key Unique identifier (filename/path) for an object within a bucket
Prefix Folder-like structure in object keys (e.g., resumes/user_123/)
Versioning Keep multiple variants of an object for recovery and rollback
Lifecycle Policy Rules to automate transition between storage classes or deletion
Pre-signed URL Temporary URL with embedded credentials for secure object access
Multipart Upload Upload large files in parts for better performance and reliability
Transfer Acceleration Use CloudFront edge locations to speed up uploads
CORS Cross-Origin Resource Sharing - allows web apps to access S3
SSE Server-Side Encryption - AWS encrypts data at rest
Glacier Low-cost archive storage class with retrieval times from minutes to hours

Storage Type Object Storage Block Storage File Storage Instance Storage

Access Method HTTP/HTTPS API Mounted to EC2 NFS mount Local filesystem

🎯 When to Use S3 for anihpj
Use S3 when:
  • ✅ Storing Django static files (CSS, JS, images)
  • ✅ User-uploaded files (resumes, logos, attachments)
  • ✅ Database backups and application archives
  • ✅ Serving files via HTTP/HTTPS API
  • ✅ Need unlimited, scalable storage
  • ✅ Want 99.999999999% durability
  • ✅ Integration with CloudFront CDN
Use EBS when:
  • ⚠️ EC2 root volumes and application data
  • ⚠️ Database storage (PostgreSQL, MySQL)
  • ⚠️ Need block-level access and low latency
Use EFS when:
  • ⚠️ Multiple EC2 instances need shared access
  • ⚠️ NFS protocol required
  • ⚠️ Concurrent read/write from multiple servers

🎓 Final Recommendation for anihpj:

Use S3 as your primary storage for all static files, user uploads, and backups. It's the most cost-effective, scalable, and durable option. Combine with CloudFront CDN for optimal performance.

Cost-Benefit: S3 costs 60-80% less than EBS/EFS while providing better durability and scalability. Perfect for Django applications with user-generated content.

Implementation Path: Local storage (Dev) → S3 (MVP) → S3 + CloudFront (Scale) → S3 + Lambda + CloudFront (Enterprise)

🗂️ Amazon EFS (Elastic File System)

Category: Storage  |  Use Case: Shared File Storage for EC2, Containers, Lambda  |  Pricing: Pay-per-GB Used + Performance Mode  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS EFS Docs

Amazon EFS provides scalable, fully managed NFS file storage for use with AWS compute services. Perfect for shared Django media files, application logs, and data that needs to be accessed concurrently from multiple EC2 instances or containers.

📋 Overview & Introduction

Amazon EFS is a fully managed NFS (Network File System) that provides shared file storage for EC2 instances, Lambda functions, and containers. It automatically scales from gigabytes to petabytes without disrupting applications.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Elastic Scaling: Automatically grows and shrinks as you add/remove files
  • High Availability: 99.999999999% (11 9's) durability across multiple AZs
  • Shared Access: Thousands of concurrent EC2 connections
  • POSIX Compliant: Standard file system interface and semantics
  • Performance: Low latency with throughput that scales with size
  • Security: Encryption at rest and in transit, VPC and IAM controls
  • Backup: Automatic daily backups with point-in-time recovery
💡 Perfect for anihpj: Share Django media files across multiple EC2 instances, store application logs from all servers, enable shared session storage, and provide consistent file access for load-balanced environments.

🔧 Core Concepts

📁 File Systems

EFS File System is the primary resource. Each file system has:

  • File System ID: Unique identifier (fs-12345678)
  • Performance Mode: General Purpose or Max I/O
  • Throughput Mode: Bursting or Provisioned
  • Storage Classes: Standard, Infrequent Access (IA)
🎯 Mount Targets

Mount Targets provide network access points:

  • IP Address: IPv4 address in your VPC
  • Security Groups: Control NFS traffic (port 2049)
  • Multi-AZ: One mount target per availability zone
  • DNS Name: Auto-generated for easy mounting
⚡ Performance Modes
General Purpose Mode
  • ✅ Low latency (sub-millisecond)
  • ✅ Up to 7,000 file operations/second
  • ✅ Best for anihpj web applications
  • ⚠️ Lower maximum throughput
Max I/O Mode
  • ✅ Higher throughput levels
  • ✅ 100+ concurrent clients
  • ✅ Analytics and data processing
  • ⚠️ Higher latencies per operation
📊 Throughput Modes
Bursting Mode
  • ✅ Default mode for most workloads
  • ✅ Baseline + burst throughput
  • 📊 50 MB/s per TiB baseline
  • ⚡ Up to 100 MB/s burst capability
  • 💰 No additional cost
Provisioned Mode
  • ✅ Consistent high throughput
  • ✅ Independent of storage size
  • 📊 Up to 1000+ MB/s available
  • ⚡ Predictable performance
  • 💰 Additional cost per MB/s
📝 anihpj Throughput Calculation
# For 260GB anihpj storage:
# Bursting mode baseline: 260GB * 50 MB/s per TiB = ~12.7 MB/s
# Burst capability: 100 MB/s (for workload spikes)
# 
# Use cases:
# - Normal web traffic: Bursting mode sufficient
# - Heavy file processing: Consider Provisioned mode
# - Cost optimization: Start with bursting, monitor performance
🔧 anihpj EFS Configuration
{
  "FileSystemPolicy": {
    "Version": "2012-10-17",
    "Statement": [
      {
        "Sid": "anihpjWebAccess",
        "Effect": "Allow",
        "Principal": {"AWS": "*"},
        "Action": [
          "elasticfilesystem:CreateFileSystem",
          "elasticfilesystem:ClientMount",
          "elasticfilesystem:ClientWrite"
        ],
        "Condition": {
          "StringEquals": {
            "elasticfilesystem:AccessPointArn": "arn:aws:elasticfilesystem:us-east-1:account:access-point/fsap-anihpj-media"
          }
        }
      }
    ]
  },
  "PerformanceMode": "generalPurpose",
  "ThroughputMode": "bursting",
  "StorageClass": "standard",
  "Tags": [
    {"Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-shared-storage"},
    {"Key": "Environment", "Value": "production"},
    {"Key": "Application", "Value": "job-portal"}
  ]
}

🚀 Getting Started

📋 Prerequisites
  • ✅ AWS CLI installed and configured
  • ✅ VPC with private subnets in multiple AZs
  • ✅ EC2 instances with NFS client installed
  • ✅ Security groups allowing NFS traffic (port 2049)
  • ✅ IAM permissions for EFS operations
🏗️ Create EFS File System
📝 AWS CLI - Create File System
# Create EFS file system for anihpj
aws efs create-file-system \
    --creation-token anihpj-shared-storage-2025 \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose \
    --throughput-mode bursting \
    --encrypted \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-shared-storage \
           Key=Environment,Value=production \
           Key=Application,Value=jobportal

# Get the file system ID
export EFS_ID=$(aws efs describe-file-systems \
    --query 'FileSystems[?Name==`anihpj-shared-storage`].FileSystemId' \
    --output text)

echo "EFS File System ID: $EFS_ID"
🎯 Create Mount Targets
📝 Create Mount Targets in Multiple AZs
# Create security group for EFS
aws ec2 create-security-group \
    --group-name anihpj-efs-sg \
    --description "Security group for anihpj EFS mount targets"

# Allow NFS traffic from EC2 security group
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-efs-sg \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 2049 \
    --source-group anihpj-web-sg

# Get subnet IDs
export SUBNET_1A=$(aws ec2 describe-subnets \
    --filters "Name=tag:Name,Values=anihpj-private-1a" \
    --query 'Subnets[0].SubnetId' --output text)

export SUBNET_1B=$(aws ec2 describe-subnets \
    --filters "Name=tag:Name,Values=anihpj-private-1b" \
    --query 'Subnets[0].SubnetId' --output text)

# Create mount targets
aws efs create-mount-target \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --subnet-id $SUBNET_1A \
    --security-groups sg-efs-anihpj

aws efs create-mount-target \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --subnet-id $SUBNET_1B \
    --security-groups sg-efs-anihpj
💿 Mount EFS on EC2 Instances
📝 Install NFS Client and Mount
# Install NFS utilities (Ubuntu/Debian)
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install -y nfs-common

# Install NFS utilities (Amazon Linux/CentOS)
sudo yum install -y nfs-utils

# Create mount directory
sudo mkdir -p /mnt/efs/anihpj

# Mount using EFS DNS name
sudo mount -t nfs4 -o nfsvers=4.1,rsize=1048576,wsize=1048576,hard,intr,timeo=600 \
    $EFS_ID.efs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com:/ /mnt/efs/anihpj

# Verify mount
df -h | grep efs

# Add to /etc/fstab for persistent mounting
echo "$EFS_ID.efs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com:/ /mnt/efs/anihpj nfs4 nfsvers=4.1,rsize=1048576,wsize=1048576,hard,intr,timeo=600 0 0" | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab
🐍 Django Integration
📝 Django Settings for EFS
# anihpj/settings.py
import os
from pathlib import Path

BASE_DIR = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent

# EFS mount point
EFS_MOUNT_PATH = '/mnt/efs/anihpj'

# Media files configuration
MEDIA_URL = '/media/'
MEDIA_ROOT = os.path.join(EFS_MOUNT_PATH, 'media')

# Static files (optional - better to use S3)
# STATIC_ROOT = os.path.join(EFS_MOUNT_PATH, 'static')

# Logging configuration
LOGGING = {
    'version': 1,
    'disable_existing_loggers': False,
    'handlers': {
        'efs_file': {
            'level': 'INFO',
            'class': 'logging.FileHandler',
            'filename': os.path.join(EFS_MOUNT_PATH, 'logs', 'django.log'),
            'formatter': 'verbose',
        },
    },
    'formatters': {
        'verbose': {
            'format': '{levelname} {asctime} {module} {process:d} {thread:d} {message}',
            'style': '{',
        },
    },
    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['efs_file'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': True,
        },
        'anihpj': {
            'handlers': ['efs_file'],
            'level': 'DEBUG',
            'propagate': True,
        },
    },
}

# Session storage on EFS (alternative to database)
SESSION_ENGINE = 'django.contrib.sessions.backends.file'
SESSION_FILE_PATH = os.path.join(EFS_MOUNT_PATH, 'sessions')
📝 anihpj Models with EFS Storage
# jobpost/models.py
import os
from django.db import models
from django.contrib.auth.models import User

def user_resume_path(instance, filename):
    """Store resumes in EFS organized by user"""
    return f'resumes/user_{instance.user.id}/{filename}'

def company_logo_path(instance, filename):
    """Store company logos in EFS"""
    return f'company_logos/{instance.slug}/{filename}'

class JobPost(models.Model):
    title = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    description = models.TextField()
    company = models.CharField(max_length=100)
    company_logo = models.ImageField(
        upload_to=company_logo_path, 
        blank=True, 
        null=True
    )
    attachment = models.FileField(
        upload_to='job_attachments/', 
        blank=True, 
        null=True
    )
    created_at = models.DateTimeField(auto_now_add=True)
    
    class Meta:
        ordering = ['-created_at']

class UserProfile(models.Model):
    user = models.OneToOneField(User, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to=user_resume_path, 
        blank=True, 
        null=True
    )
    profile_image = models.ImageField(
        upload_to='profile_images/', 
        blank=True, 
        null=True
    )
    
    def __str__(self):
        return f"{self.user.username}'s Profile"

✨ Key Features

🔑 Access Points

Access Points provide application-specific entry points with custom permissions:

  • Path-based Access: Restrict access to specific directories
  • POSIX Permissions: Set user/group ownership and permissions
  • Root Directory: Create isolated environments
  • Creation Policy: Auto-create directories with specific permissions
📝 Create Access Points for anihpj
# Access point for media files
aws efs create-access-point \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --posix-user Uid=1000,Gid=1000 \
    --root-directory Path="/media",CreationInfo='{OwnerUid=1000,OwnerGid=1000,Permissions=755}' \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-media-access

# Access point for logs
aws efs create-access-point \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --posix-user Uid=1000,Gid=1000 \
    --root-directory Path="/logs",CreationInfo='{OwnerUid=1000,OwnerGid=1000,Permissions=755}' \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-logs-access

# Access point for backups (read-only for some users)
aws efs create-access-point \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --posix-user Uid=1000,Gid=1000 \
    --root-directory Path="/backups",CreationInfo='{OwnerUid=1000,OwnerGid=1000,Permissions=644}' \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-backups-access
♻️ Lifecycle Management

Intelligent Tiering automatically moves files to lower-cost storage:

  • Standard Storage: Frequently accessed files
  • Infrequent Access (IA): Files not accessed for 30+ days
  • Cost Savings: Up to 92% reduction for IA storage
  • Automatic: No application changes needed
📝 Configure Lifecycle Policy
# Enable lifecycle management
aws efs put-lifecycle-configuration \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --lifecycle-policies TransitionToIA=AFTER_30_DAYS,TransitionToPrimaryStorageClass=AFTER_1_ACCESS

# View lifecycle configuration
aws efs describe-lifecycle-configuration --file-system-id $EFS_ID

# Example cost analysis for anihpj
# Standard Storage: $0.30/GB/month
# IA Storage: $0.025/GB/month (92% savings)
# Estimated savings: $0.275/GB for files >30 days old
🚀 Performance Modes

Performance Modes optimize for different workload patterns:

Performance Mode Max Operations/sec Max IOPS Latency anihpj Use Case
General Purpose 7,000 7,000 Low Web uploads, user files
Max I/O 500,000+ 500,000+ Higher Bulk processing, analytics
📝 Monitor Performance Metrics
# Check current performance mode
aws efs describe-file-systems \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --query 'FileSystems[0].PerformanceMode'

# Monitor throughput utilization
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name ThroughputUtilization \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time $(date -d '1 hour ago' --iso-8601) \
    --end-time $(date --iso-8601) \
    --period 300 \
    --statistics Average
⚡ Throughput Modes

Throughput Modes control bandwidth allocation:

📊 Throughput Performance Comparison
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    EFS Throughput Modes                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  BURSTING MODE (Default)                                        │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Base: 50 MB/s per TB stored                           │    │
│  │  Burst: Up to 100 MB/s (baseline credits)              │    │
│  │  Cost: No additional charges                           │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  PROVISIONED MODE                                              │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Consistent: Set throughput regardless of size         │    │
│  │  Range: 1 MB/s to 1,024 MB/s                          │    │
│  │  Cost: $6.00 per MB/s/month                           │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  ANIHPJ RECOMMENDATION: Start with Bursting                   │
│  ├─ Expected storage: 10-50 GB                                │
│  ├─ Base throughput: 2.5 MB/s (sufficient for uploads)       │
│  └─ Burst available: 100 MB/s for peak traffic               │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
📝 Configure Throughput Mode
# Create EFS with provisioned throughput (if needed)
aws efs create-file-system \
    --creation-token anihpj-provisioned-$(date +%s) \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose \
    --throughput-mode provisioned \
    --provisioned-throughput-in-mibps 10 \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-efs-provisioned \
           Key=Environment,Value=production \
           Key=Application,Value=anihpj-jobpost

# Modify existing EFS throughput
aws efs modify-file-system \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --throughput-mode provisioned \
    --provisioned-throughput-in-mibps 5

# Monitor throughput metrics
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name TotalIOBytes \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time $(date -d '24 hours ago' --iso-8601) \
    --end-time $(date --iso-8601) \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Sum
💾 Backup & Restore

AWS Backup Integration provides comprehensive data protection:

  • Automatic Backups: Daily, weekly, monthly schedules
  • Point-in-Time Recovery: Restore to any previous backup
  • Cross-Region Backup: Disaster recovery across regions
  • Compliance: Meet data retention requirements
📝 Enable EFS Backup
# Enable automatic backups
aws efs put-backup-policy \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --backup-policy Status=ENABLED

# Create backup vault for anihpj
aws backup create-backup-vault \
    --backup-vault-name anihpj-efs-backups \
    --encryption-key-arn arn:aws:kms:us-east-1:account:key/key-id

# Create backup plan
aws backup create-backup-plan \
    --backup-plan '{
        "BackupPlanName": "anihpj-efs-daily-backup",
        "Rules": [{
            "RuleName": "DailyBackups",
            "TargetBackupVault": "anihpj-efs-backups",
            "ScheduleExpression": "cron(0 5 ? * * *)",
            "StartWindowMinutes": 480,
            "CompletionWindowMinutes": 10080,
            "Lifecycle": {
                "DeleteAfterDays": 30,
                "MoveToColdStorageAfterDays": 7
            }
        }]
    }'
🔒 Encryption & Security

End-to-End Encryption protects data at all levels:

  • Encryption at Rest: AES-256 encryption using AWS KMS
  • Encryption in Transit: TLS 1.2 for NFS connections
  • Key Management: AWS managed or customer managed keys
  • Access Control: IAM policies and POSIX permissions
📝 Mount with Encryption in Transit
# Install EFS utilities for encryption
sudo apt-get install -y amazon-efs-utils

# Mount with encryption in transit
sudo mount -t efs -o tls $EFS_ID:/ /mnt/efs/anihpj

# Mount with access point and encryption
sudo mount -t efs -o tls,accesspoint=fsap-anihpj-media $EFS_ID:/ /mnt/efs/anihpj/media
📈 Elastic Scaling

Automatic Scaling without capacity planning:

  • Petabyte Scale: Grows and shrinks automatically
  • No Provisioning: Pay only for storage used
  • Instant Access: Available immediately after creation
  • Performance Scales: Throughput increases with size
📝 anihpj Scaling Example
# Django model for handling growing file storage
from django.db import models
from django.core.files.storage import default_storage

class JobApplication(models.Model):
    applicant = models.ForeignKey('User', on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    job_posting = models.ForeignKey('JobPosting', on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to='resumes/%Y/%m/',  # Organized by date on EFS
        storage=default_storage      # Uses EFS via django-storages
    )
    cover_letter = models.FileField(
        upload_to='cover_letters/%Y/%m/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )

    def save(self, *args, **kwargs):
        # EFS automatically scales to accommodate new files
        super().save(*args, **kwargs)
        
        # Log storage metrics for monitoring
        if self.resume:
            print(f"Resume stored on EFS: {self.resume.path}")
            # EFS handles the scaling automatically

📝 anihpj Security Configuration
{
  "fileSystemPolicy": {
    "Version": "2012-10-17",
    "Statement": [
      {
        "Sid": "anihpjApplicationAccess",
        "Effect": "Allow",
        "Principal": {
          "AWS": "arn:aws:iam::account:role/anihpj-ec2-role"
        },
        "Action": [
          "elasticfilesystem:ClientMount",
          "elasticfilesystem:ClientWrite"
        ],
        "Resource": "*",
        "Condition": {
          "Bool": {
            "aws:SecureTransport": "true"
          },
          "StringEquals": {
            "elasticfilesystem:AccessPointArn": "arn:aws:elasticfilesystem:region:account:access-point/fsap-anihpj-media"
          }
        }
      }
    ]
  }
}

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

💳 Pricing Model
Standard Storage
$0.30/GB-month
  • Frequently accessed files
  • Low latency access
  • No minimum storage duration
  • No retrieval fees
Infrequent Access (IA)
$0.025/GB-month
  • Files accessed < once per month
  • 92% cost reduction
  • $0.01/GB retrieval fee
  • 30-day minimum storage
📊 anihpj Cost Breakdown
Storage Type Size (GB) Price/GB Monthly Cost Use Case
Media Files (Standard) 50 GB $0.30 $15.00 Active resumes, logos
Logs (Standard) 10 GB $0.30 $3.00 Application logs
Archive (IA) 200 GB $0.025 $5.00 Old files, backups
Throughput - Bursting $0.00 Included in storage
Total Monthly Cost ~$23.00 260 GB total
🎯 Cost Optimization Strategies
🔄 Lifecycle Management
  • Automatic Tiering: Move old files to IA storage after 30 days
  • Cost Impact: 92% reduction for archived files
  • Implementation: Set lifecycle policy on file system creation
  • anihpj Savings: ~$165/month on 200GB of old resumes
📁 Storage Classes Comparison
Storage Class Cost/GB/Month Retrieval Cost Min Duration Best For
Standard $0.30 $0.00 None Active files, uploads
IA (Infrequent Access) $0.025 $0.01/GB 30 days Backup, archive files

│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  260GB gp3: ~$21/month                                 │    │
│  │  ❌ Single EC2 attachment                              │    │
│  │  ❌ Manual backup management                           │    │
│  │  ❌ No cross-AZ sharing                                │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  S3 (Object storage)                                          │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  260GB Standard: ~$6/month                             │    │
│  │  ❌ No POSIX file system                               │    │
│  │  ❌ API-only access                                    │    │
│  │  ✅ Cheapest option                                    │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  RECOMMENDATION: EFS provides best balance                     │
│  └─ Shared access needed for multi-instance deployments       │

📝 Cost Monitoring & Optimization
# Monitor storage usage and costs
aws efs describe-file-systems \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --query 'FileSystems[0].SizeInBytes'

# Get detailed storage metrics
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name StorageBytes \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID Name=StorageClass,Value=Standard \
    --start-time $(date -d '30 days ago' --iso-8601) \
    --end-time $(date --iso-8601) \
    --period 86400 \
    --statistics Average

# Cost optimization script for anihpj
#!/bin/bash
EFS_ID="fs-yourfsid"
CURRENT_SIZE=$(aws efs describe-file-systems \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --query 'FileSystems[0].SizeInBytes.Value' \
    --output text)

# Convert bytes to GB
SIZE_GB=$((CURRENT_SIZE / 1024 / 1024 / 1024))
MONTHLY_COST=$(echo "scale=2; $SIZE_GB * 0.30" | bc)

echo "Current EFS Size: ${SIZE_GB} GB"
echo "Estimated Monthly Cost: \$${MONTHLY_COST}"

# Check if lifecycle policy is enabled
LIFECYCLE=$(aws efs describe-lifecycle-configuration \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --output text 2>/dev/null)

if [ -z "$LIFECYCLE" ]; then
    echo "⚠️  Lifecycle policy not configured - potential savings available"
    POTENTIAL_SAVINGS=$(echo "scale=2; $SIZE_GB * 0.275" | bc)
    echo "💰 Potential monthly savings with IA: \$${POTENTIAL_SAVINGS}"
fi
1. Enable Intelligent Tiering

Automatically move infrequently accessed files to IA storage class.

aws efs put-lifecycle-configuration \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --lifecycle-policies TransitionToIA=AFTER_30_DAYS
2. Use Regional Storage Classes

Choose One Zone storage class for non-critical data (47% cost reduction).

# Create One Zone file system
aws efs create-file-system \
    --availability-zone-name us-east-1a \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose
3. Monitor Storage Usage

Use CloudWatch metrics to track storage consumption and optimize.

# Get storage metrics
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name StorageBytes \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time 2025-10-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2025-11-01T00:00:00Z \
    --period 86400 \
    --statistics Average
4. Implement File Retention Policies

Automatically delete old log files and temporary data.

# Django management command for cleanup
# anihpj/management/commands/cleanup_efs.py
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand
import os
import time
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

class Command(BaseCommand):
    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        # Clean logs older than 30 days
        log_dir = '/mnt/efs/anihpj/logs'
        cutoff = time.time() - (30 * 24 * 60 * 60)
        
        for filename in os.listdir(log_dir):
            filepath = os.path.join(log_dir, filename)
            if os.path.getmtime(filepath) < cutoff:
                os.remove(filepath)
                self.stdout.write(f'Deleted: {filename}')
⚠️ Cost Comparison:

EFS is ~3x more expensive than S3 for storage, but provides POSIX file system access. Use EFS only when you need shared file access across multiple instances. For static files and backups, S3 is more cost-effective.

📈 Scalability & High Availability

🔄 Automatic Scaling

Elastic Scaling: EFS automatically scales storage capacity up or down as you add or remove files.

  • No Provisioning: No need to provision storage capacity in advance
  • Petabyte Scale: Scales to petabytes automatically
  • Performance Scaling: Throughput scales with storage size
  • Instant Availability: New capacity available immediately
🌐 Multi-AZ Deployment

Regional Storage: Data is stored redundantly across multiple Availability Zones.

  • 99.999999999% Durability: Designed for 11 9's durability
  • 99.99% Availability: High availability SLA
  • Automatic Replication: Data replicated across AZs
  • No Single Point of Failure: AZ failures don't affect availability

💡 Scaling Strategy for anihpj:

Start with General Purpose mode for low latency. As your job portal grows and requires higher throughput for media processing, consider switching to Max I/O mode or using Provisioned Throughput.

📊 Auto-Scaling

Automatic Scaling Features:

  • Storage Scaling: Automatically grows and shrinks with usage
  • Performance Scaling: Throughput increases as file system grows
  • No Downtime: Scaling happens transparently
  • No Configuration: Zero administrative overhead
📝 anihpj Auto-Scaling Example
# Django management command to monitor EFS growth
import os
import subprocess
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Monitor EFS storage usage for anihpj'

    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        efs_path = '/mnt/efs/anihpj'
        
        # Check current usage
        result = subprocess.run(['df', '-h', efs_path], 
                              capture_output=True, text=True)
        
        # EFS shows as a large number, but actual billing is for used space
        media_size = self.get_directory_size(f"{efs_path}/media")
        logs_size = self.get_directory_size(f"{efs_path}/logs")
        
        self.stdout.write(f"Media files: {media_size / (1024**3):.2f} GB")
        self.stdout.write(f"Log files: {logs_size / (1024**3):.2f} GB")
        self.stdout.write("EFS automatically scales - no action needed!")

    def get_directory_size(self, path):
        total_size = 0
        for dirpath, dirnames, filenames in os.walk(path):
            for filename in filenames:
                filepath = os.path.join(dirpath, filename)
                total_size += os.path.getsize(filepath)
        return total_size

🔬 Advanced Topics

🚀 Provisioned Throughput

Provisioned Throughput Mode provides consistent performance independent of storage size:

  • Guaranteed Performance: Consistent throughput regardless of data size
  • Predictable Costs: Pay for provisioned throughput
  • High Performance: Up to 1 GiB/s for small file systems
  • Use Case: Performance-critical applications
📝 Enable Provisioned Throughput
# Modify file system to use provisioned throughput
aws efs modify-file-system \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --throughput-mode provisioned \
    --provisioned-throughput-in-mibps 500

# Monitor throughput utilization
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name TotalIOBytes \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time 2025-11-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2025-11-02T00:00:00Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Sum
🌍 Cross-Region Replication

Cross-Region Replication provides disaster recovery capabilities:

  • Disaster Recovery: Automatic failover to another region
  • Low RPO: Recovery Point Objective of 15 minutes
  • Automatic Sync: Changes replicated continuously
  • Cost Effective: Replicated data stored in IA class
📝 Setup Cross-Region Replication
# Create replication configuration
aws efs create-replication-configuration \
    --source-file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --destinations Region=us-west-2,KmsKeyId=arn:aws:kms:us-west-2:account:key/key-id,AvailabilityZoneName=us-west-2a

# Monitor replication status
aws efs describe-replication-configurations \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID
⚡ Lambda Integration

Lambda + EFS enables serverless file processing:

  • Shared Storage: Lambda functions access same files
  • Large Files: Process files larger than Lambda's /tmp limit
  • Persistent Data: Data persists between Lambda invocations
  • Machine Learning: Shared model files and datasets
📝 Lambda Function with EFS
# anihpj_image_processor.py - Lambda function
import json
import os
from PIL import Image
import boto3

# EFS mount point in Lambda
EFS_MOUNT_PATH = '/mnt/efs'

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """
    Process uploaded company logos and create thumbnails
    Files are stored in EFS for persistent access
    """
    
    # Get file info from S3 event
    bucket = event['Records'][0]['s3']['bucket']['name']
    key = event['Records'][0]['s3']['object']['key']
    
    if not key.startswith('company_logos/'):
        return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Not a company logo'}
    
    # Download from S3 to EFS
    s3 = boto3.client('s3')
    local_path = f"{EFS_MOUNT_PATH}/temp/{key}"
    os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(local_path), exist_ok=True)
    
    s3.download_file(bucket, key, local_path)
    
    # Create thumbnail
    with Image.open(local_path) as image:
        # Create 150x150 thumbnail
        thumbnail = image.copy()
        thumbnail.thumbnail((150, 150), Image.Resampling.LANCZOS)
        
        # Save thumbnail to EFS
        thumb_path = f"{EFS_MOUNT_PATH}/thumbnails/{key}"
        os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(thumb_path), exist_ok=True)
        thumbnail.save(thumb_path)
        
        # Upload thumbnail back to S3
        s3.upload_file(thumb_path, bucket, f"thumbnails/{key}")
    
    # Clean up temp file
    os.remove(local_path)
    
    return {
        'statusCode': 200,
        'body': json.dumps(f'Processed {key}')
    }

📝 Kubernetes StorageClass and PVC
# storage-class.yaml
apiVersion: storage.k8s.io/v1
kind: StorageClass
metadata:
  name: anihpj-efs-sc
provisioner: efs.csi.aws.com
parameters:
  provisioningMode: efs-ap
  fileSystemId: fs-yourfsid
  directoryPerms: "700"
  gidRangeStart: "1000"
  gidRangeEnd: "2000"
  basePath: "/anihpj-k8s"

---
# pvc.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
metadata:
  name: anihpj-efs-claim
spec:
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteMany
  storageClassName: anihpj-efs-sc
  resources:
    requests:
      storage: 5Gi

---
# deployment.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-app
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-django
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-django
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django
        image: anihpj/webapp:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        volumeMounts:
        - name: efs-storage
          mountPath: /app/media
        env:
        - name: MEDIA_ROOT
          value: "/app/media"
      volumes:
      - name: efs-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-efs-claim

⚡ Performance Optimization Techniques

Advanced Performance Tuning for high-throughput workloads:

Optimization Configuration Impact anihpj Use Case
Read/Write Buffer Size rsize=1048576, wsize=1048576 +20-30% throughput Large file uploads
Connection Timeout timeo=600 Better reliability Web server stability
Retransmission Count retrans=2 Faster failure detection Quick error recovery
Hard Mount hard Prevents data loss Critical for database files
📝 Optimal Mount Command for anihpj
# Production-optimized mount for anihpj
sudo mount -t nfs4 -o nfsvers=4.1,rsize=1048576,wsize=1048576,hard,intr,timeo=600,retrans=2,_netdev,fsc \
    $EFS_ID.efs.$AWS_REGION.amazonaws.com:/ /mnt/efs/anihpj

# Performance monitoring
iostat -x 1 5  # Monitor I/O performance
nfsstat -c     # NFS client statistics
df -h          # Check mount and space usage
📍 One Zone Storage Classes

One Zone Storage Classes provide cost optimization for non-critical workloads:

Storage Class Availability Cost Savings anihpj Use Case
Regional Standard Multi-AZ Baseline Production media files
One Zone Single AZ 47% cheaper Development, testing
One Zone-IA Single AZ 68% cheaper Archive, backup data
📝 Create One Zone EFS for Development
# Create One Zone EFS for anihpj development environment
aws efs create-file-system \
    --creation-token anihpj-dev-$(date +%s) \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose \
    --throughput-mode bursting \
    --availability-zone-name us-east-1a \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-dev-efs \
           Key=Environment,Value=development \
           Key=CostOptimization,Value=one-zone

# Cost comparison for anihpj development (50GB)
# Regional: $15/month
# One Zone: $8/month (47% savings)
# Potential annual savings: $84
  • Cost Savings: Up to 47% lower cost than Regional
  • Single AZ Storage: Data stored in one Availability Zone
  • Same Performance: Identical performance to Regional
  • Use Cases: Development, testing, non-critical data
Storage Class Durability Availability Cost/GB (Standard) anihpj Use Case
Regional 99.999999999% 99.99% $0.30 ✅ Production media files
One Zone 99.999999999%* 99.9% $0.16 ✅ Development environment
✅ Temporary processing files

*Within a single AZ. If the AZ becomes unavailable, data is inaccessible.

📝 Create One Zone File System
# Create One Zone EFS for anihpj development
aws efs create-file-system \
    --creation-token anihpj-dev-one-zone-$(date +%s) \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose \
    --throughput-mode bursting \
    --availability-zone-name us-east-1a \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-dev-one-zone \
           Key=Environment,Value=development \
           Key=CostOptimized,Value=true

# Create mount target in the same AZ
aws efs create-mount-target \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --subnet-id subnet-development-1a \
    --security-groups sg-efs-dev
⚠️ One Zone Considerations:
  • Data is only available within the specified AZ
  • If AZ fails, data becomes temporarily inaccessible
  • Cannot create mount targets in other AZs
  • Best for non-critical, replaceable data

⭐ Best Practices

🔒 Security Best Practices
1. Use VPC and Security Groups
  • ✅ Deploy EFS in private subnets
  • ✅ Restrict NFS traffic to specific security groups
  • ✅ Use VPC endpoints for AWS API calls
  • ❌ Never expose EFS to public internet
2. Enable Encryption
  • ✅ Enable encryption at rest for sensitive data
  • ✅ Use encryption in transit for production
  • ✅ Use customer-managed KMS keys for compliance
  • ✅ Rotate encryption keys regularly
3. Implement Access Controls
  • ✅ Use Access Points for application-specific access
  • ✅ Set proper POSIX permissions
  • ✅ Implement IAM policies for API access
  • ✅ Use file system policies for resource-based access
⚡ Performance Best Practices
1. Choose Right Performance Mode
  • ✅ General Purpose for most anihpj workloads
  • ✅ Max I/O for high concurrent access
  • ✅ Monitor CloudWatch metrics for optimization
  • ⚠️ Test both modes with your workload
2. Optimize Mount Options
# Optimized mount options for anihpj
sudo mount -t nfs4 -o nfsvers=4.1,rsize=1048576,wsize=1048576,hard,intr,timeo=600,retrans=2 \
    $EFS_ID.efs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com:/ /mnt/efs
3. Use Regional vs One Zone Appropriately
  • ✅ Regional for production workloads
  • ✅ One Zone for development/testing (cost savings)
  • ✅ One Zone for non-critical data
💰 Cost Optimization Practices
1. Enable Intelligent Tiering
# Enable lifecycle management for cost savings
aws efs put-lifecycle-configuration \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --lifecycle-policies TransitionToIA=AFTER_30_DAYS
2. Monitor and Clean Up
  • ✅ Set up CloudWatch alarms for storage usage
  • ✅ Implement automated cleanup for temporary files

            "TargetBackupVault": "default",
            "ScheduleExpression": "cron(0 2 ? * * *)",
            "Lifecycle": {
                "MoveToColdStorageAfterDays": 30,
                "DeleteAfterDays": 365

    }'

import os
import json
from pathlib import Path

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """Process uploaded resumes on EFS"""
    efs_mount = "/mnt/efs"
    
    # Process files from EFS
    resume_dir = Path(efs_mount) / "anihpj" / "media" / "resumes"
    
    for resume_file in resume_dir.glob("*.pdf"):
        # Process resume (extract text, analyze, etc.)
        process_resume(resume_file)
    
    return {
        'statusCode': 200,
        'body': json.dumps('Processing completed')
    }

🐍 Django-Specific Best Practices
1. File Upload Handling
# anihpj/models.py - Optimized file handling
import os
from django.db import models
from django.core.files.storage import default_storage

class JobPost(models.Model):
    def attachment_upload_path(instance, filename):
        """Organize files by date and job ID"""
        return f'job_attachments/{instance.created_at.year}/{instance.created_at.month}/{instance.id}/{filename}'
    
    attachment = models.FileField(
        upload_to=attachment_upload_path,
        blank=True,
        null=True,
        help_text="Stored on EFS for multi-instance access"
    )
    
    def save(self, *args, **kwargs):
        # Ensure directory exists on EFS
        if self.attachment:
            upload_path = os.path.dirname(self.attachment.name)
            full_path = os.path.join(default_storage.location, upload_path)
            os.makedirs(full_path, exist_ok=True)
        
        super().save(*args, **kwargs)

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import pandas as pd
import os
from datetime import datetime

# Shared data directory on EFS
DATA_DIR = '/analytics/data'

def process_job_applications():
    """Process job application data from shared storage"""
    
    # Read raw data (written by Django app)
    raw_data = pd.read_csv(f'{DATA_DIR}/raw_logs/applications.csv')
    
    # Process data
    processed = raw_data.groupby(['company', 'job_title']).size()
    
    # Save results (accessible to all instances)
    timestamp = datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')
    processed.to_csv(f'{DATA_DIR}/reports/job_trends_{timestamp}.csv')
    
    print(f"Processed {len(raw_data)} applications")

if __name__ == '__main__':
    process_job_applications()

📁 Content Management

📝 Document Management System
# anihpj/document_manager.py
import os
import shutil
from datetime import datetime
from django.conf import settings

class EFSDocumentManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.efs_root = '/mnt/efs/anihpj'
        self.documents_path = os.path.join(self.efs_root, 'documents')
        self.versions_path = os.path.join(self.efs_root, 'versions')
        
    def store_resume(self, user_id, file_obj, filename):
        """Store resume with version control"""
        user_dir = os.path.join(self.documents_path, 'resumes', str(user_id))
        os.makedirs(user_dir, exist_ok=True)
        
        # Store current version
        file_path = os.path.join(user_dir, filename)
        
        # Create version backup if file exists
        if os.path.exists(file_path):
            timestamp = datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')
            version_dir = os.path.join(self.versions_path, str(user_id))
            os.makedirs(version_dir, exist_ok=True)
            
            version_file = f"{timestamp}_{filename}"
            shutil.copy2(file_path, os.path.join(version_dir, version_file))
        
        # Save new file
        with open(file_path, 'wb') as f:
            for chunk in file_obj.chunks():
                f.write(chunk)
                
        return file_path
    
    def get_resume_versions(self, user_id):
        """Get all versions of user's resume"""
        version_dir = os.path.join(self.versions_path, str(user_id))
        
        if not os.path.exists(version_dir):
            return []
            
        versions = []
        for filename in os.listdir(version_dir):
            file_path = os.path.join(version_dir, filename)
            stat = os.stat(file_path)
            versions.append({
                'filename': filename,
                'size': stat.st_size,
                'modified': datetime.fromtimestamp(stat.st_mtime)
            })
            
        return sorted(versions, key=lambda x: x['modified'], reverse=True)
