📝 CI/CD with EFS
# .github/workflows/deploy.yml
name: Deploy anihpj to EFS-enabled infrastructure

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: self-hosted  # EC2 with EFS mounted
    
    steps:
    - name: Checkout code
      uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: |
        python -m venv /mnt/efs/envs/anihpj
        source /mnt/efs/envs/anihpj/bin/activate
        pip install -r requirements.txt
        
    - name: Run tests with shared test data
      run: |
        source /mnt/efs/envs/anihpj/bin/activate
        # Use shared test fixtures from EFS
        export TEST_DATA_PATH=/mnt/efs/test_data
        python manage.py test
        
    - name: Deploy to shared application directory
      run: |
        # Deploy to EFS for all instances to pick up
        rsync -av --delete . /mnt/efs/applications/anihpj/
        
    - name: Store deployment artifacts
      run: |
        # Store deployment info accessible to all instances
        echo "$(date): Deployed commit $(git rev-parse HEAD)" >> /mnt/efs/logs/deployments.log
💡 Choosing the Right Use Case:

Use EFS when you need POSIX file system semantics and concurrent access from multiple instances. For simple object storage, S3 is more cost-effective. For high-performance databases, use EBS.

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

❗ Common Issues
Issue: Mount Operation Times Out

Symptoms: mount.nfs4: Connection timed out

Causes:

  • Security group not allowing NFS traffic (port 2049)
  • Network ACLs blocking traffic
  • Mount target not available in the AZ
  • DNS resolution issues

Solutions:

# Check security group rules
aws ec2 describe-security-groups --group-ids sg-your-efs-sg

# Verify mount target status
aws efs describe-mount-targets --file-system-id $EFS_ID

# Test connectivity
telnet $EFS_ID.efs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com 2049

# Use IP address instead of DNS
mount -t nfs4 -o nfsvers=4.1 10.0.1.100:/ /mnt/efs
Issue: Permission Denied Errors

Symptoms: Permission denied when accessing files

Causes:

  • Incorrect POSIX permissions
  • UID/GID mismatch between instances
  • Access Point misconfiguration
  • File system policy restrictions

Solutions:

# Check current permissions
ls -la /mnt/efs/anihpj/

# Fix ownership (run as root)
sudo chown -R 1000:1000 /mnt/efs/anihpj/media/
sudo chmod -R 755 /mnt/efs/anihpj/media/

# Use Access Point with proper POSIX settings
aws efs create-access-point \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --posix-user Uid=1000,Gid=1000 \
    --root-directory Path="/media",CreationInfo='{OwnerUid=1000,OwnerGid=1000,Permissions=755}'
Issue: Slow Performance

Symptoms: High latency, low throughput

Causes:

  • General Purpose mode with high metadata operations
  • Small file system size (limited burst credits)
  • Network connectivity issues
  • Inefficient mount options

Solutions:

# Check performance metrics
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name TotalIOTime \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time 2025-11-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2025-11-02T00:00:00Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average

# Optimize mount options
sudo umount /mnt/efs
sudo mount -t nfs4 -o nfsvers=4.1,rsize=1048576,wsize=1048576,hard,intr,timeo=600 \
    $EFS_ID.efs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com:/ /mnt/efs

# Consider Max I/O mode for high concurrency
aws efs modify-file-system \
    --file-system-id $EFS_ID \
    --performance-mode maxIO
📊 Monitoring & Diagnostics

Key CloudWatch Metrics:

  • StorageBytes: Total storage used
  • TotalIOBytes: Total I/O operations
  • ClientConnections: Number of connected clients
  • TotalIOTime: Average I/O time
  • PercentIOLimit: Percentage of I/O limit used

❓ Frequently Asked Questions
Q: Can I use EFS with Windows instances?

A: No, EFS only supports Linux-based instances. For Windows, use Amazon FSx for Windows File Server.

Q: What's the difference between EFS and EBS?

A: EFS is network-attached storage (NAS) that can be mounted by multiple instances, while EBS is block storage that attaches to a single instance.

Q: Can I access EFS from on-premises?

A: Yes, using AWS Direct Connect or VPN connections. You can mount EFS from on-premises systems.

Q: How do I migrate data from EBS to EFS?

A: Use AWS DataSync, rsync, or simple copy commands to transfer data from EBS-mounted directories to EFS.

📚 API & CLI Reference

🖥️ AWS CLI Commands
File System Management
# Create file system
aws efs create-file-system \
    --creation-token unique-token \
    --performance-mode generalPurpose \
    --throughput-mode bursting \
    --encrypted \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-efs

# List file systems
aws efs describe-file-systems

# Modify file system
aws efs modify-file-system \
    --file-system-id fs-12345678 \
    --throughput-mode provisioned \
    --provisioned-throughput-in-mibps 500

# Delete file system
aws efs delete-file-system --file-system-id fs-12345678
Mount Target Management
# Create mount target
aws efs create-mount-target \
    --file-system-id fs-12345678 \
    --subnet-id subnet-12345678 \
    --security-groups sg-12345678

# List mount targets
aws efs describe-mount-targets --file-system-id fs-12345678

# Delete mount target
aws efs delete-mount-target --mount-target-id fsmt-12345678
Access Point Management
# Create access point
aws efs create-access-point \
    --file-system-id fs-12345678 \
    --posix-user Uid=1000,Gid=1000 \
    --root-directory Path="/secure",CreationInfo='{OwnerUid=1000,OwnerGid=1000,Permissions=755}' \
    --tags Key=Name,Value=anihpj-secure-access

# List access points
aws efs describe-access-points --file-system-id fs-12345678

# Delete access point
aws efs delete-access-point --access-point-id fsap-12345678
🐍 SDK Examples
📝 Python (Boto3) Examples
import boto3
from botocore.exceptions import ClientError

# Create EFS client
efs_client = boto3.client('efs', region_name='us-east-1')

def create_anihpj_efs():
    """Create EFS file system for anihpj"""
    try:
        response = efs_client.create_file_system(
            CreationToken='anihpj-efs-2025',
            PerformanceMode='generalPurpose',
            ThroughputMode='bursting',
            Encrypted=True,
            Tags=[
                {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': 'anihpj-shared-storage'},
                {'Key': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'},
                {'Key': 'Application', 'Value': 'jobportal'}
            ]
        )
        return response['FileSystemId']
    except ClientError as e:
        print(f"Error creating EFS: {e}")
        return None

def create_access_point(file_system_id, path, uid=1000, gid=1000):
    """Create access point for specific directory"""
    try:
        response = efs_client.create_access_point(
            FileSystemId=file_system_id,
            PosixUser={
                'Uid': uid,
                'Gid': gid
            },
            RootDirectory={
                'Path': path,
                'CreationInfo': {
                    'OwnerUid': uid,
                    'OwnerGid': gid,
                    'Permissions': '755'
                }
            },
            Tags=[
                {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': f'anihpj-{path.strip("/")}-access'}
            ]
        )
        return response['AccessPointId']
    except ClientError as e:
        print(f"Error creating access point: {e}")
        return None

def monitor_efs_usage(file_system_id):
    """Monitor EFS storage usage"""
    cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1')
    
    try:
        response = cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(
            Namespace='AWS/EFS',
            MetricName='StorageBytes',
            Dimensions=[
                {'Name': 'FileSystemId', 'Value': file_system_id},
                {'Name': 'StorageClass', 'Value': 'Standard'}
            ],
            StartTime=datetime.utcnow() - timedelta(days=1),
            EndTime=datetime.utcnow(),
            Period=3600,
            Statistics=['Average']
        )
        
        if response['Datapoints']:
            latest = max(response['Datapoints'], key=lambda x: x['Timestamp'])
            storage_gb = latest['Average'] / (1024**3)
            return f"Current storage usage: {storage_gb:.2f} GB"
        else:
            return "No storage data available"
            
    except ClientError as e:
        return f"Error getting metrics: {e}"

# Usage example
if __name__ == '__main__':
    # Create file system
    fs_id = create_anihpj_efs()
    if fs_id:
        print(f"Created EFS: {fs_id}")
        
        # Create access points
        media_ap = create_access_point(fs_id, '/media')
        logs_ap = create_access_point(fs_id, '/logs')
        
        print(f"Created access points: {media_ap}, {logs_ap}")
        
        # Monitor usage
        usage = monitor_efs_usage(fs_id)
        print(usage)

⚡ Lambda Integration

Serverless File Processing: Lambda functions can access EFS for large file operations.

  • VPC Configuration: Lambda must be in same VPC as EFS
  • Access Points: Use access points for security and isolation
  • Cold Start Impact: EFS mounting adds to cold start time
  • Concurrent Access: Multiple Lambda functions can access same files
📝 Lambda Function with EFS
# lambda_function.py - Resume processing
import json
import os
import PyPDF2
import boto3
from pathlib import Path

# EFS mount point
EFS_PATH = '/mnt/efs'

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """
    Process uploaded resumes and extract text for search
    Input: S3 event with uploaded resume
    Output: Extracted text stored in EFS for search indexing
    """
    
    # Parse S3 event
    s3_event = event['Records'][0]['s3']
    bucket = s3_event['bucket']['name']
    key = s3_event['object']['key']
    
    if not key.startswith('resumes/'):
        return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Not a resume file'}
    
    # Download resume from S3 to EFS
    s3_client = boto3.client('s3')
    local_path = os.path.join(EFS_PATH, 'processing', key)
    os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(local_path), exist_ok=True)
    
    s3_client.download_file(bucket, key, local_path)
    
    try:
        # Extract text from PDF
        text_content = extract_text_from_pdf(local_path)
        
        # Store extracted text in EFS for search indexing
        text_path = os.path.join(EFS_PATH, 'extracted_text', f"{key}.txt")
        os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(text_path), exist_ok=True)
        
        with open(text_path, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
            f.write(text_content)
        
        # Store metadata for search service
        metadata = {
            'original_file': key,
            'text_file': text_path,
            'processed_at': context.aws_request_id,
            'word_count': len(text_content.split())
        }
        
        metadata_path = os.path.join(EFS_PATH, 'metadata', f"{key}.json")
        os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(metadata_path), exist_ok=True)
        
        with open(metadata_path, 'w') as f:
            json.dump(metadata, f)
        
        return {
            'statusCode': 200,
            'body': json.dumps({
                'message': f'Processed {key}',
                'word_count': metadata['word_count'],
                'text_file': text_path
            })
        }
        
    except Exception as e:
        return {
            'statusCode': 500,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': str(e)})
        }
    
    finally:
        # Clean up temporary file
        if os.path.exists(local_path):
            os.remove(local_path)

def extract_text_from_pdf(file_path):
    """Extract text from PDF file"""
    text = ""
    
    with open(file_path, 'rb') as file:
        pdf_reader = PyPDF2.PdfReader(file)
        
        for page in pdf_reader.pages:
            text += page.extract_text() + "\n"
    
    return text.strip()

Container Storage: EFS provides persistent storage for containerized applications.

  • Task Definitions: Define EFS volumes in task definitions
  • Access Points: Use access points for container isolation
  • Fargate Support: Native support in Fargate tasks
  • Multi-Container: Share data between containers in same task

📊 CloudWatch Integration

Enhanced Monitoring: Deep insights into EFS performance and usage.

  • CloudWatch Metrics: Storage, I/O, and performance metrics
  • CloudWatch Logs: EFS access logs and audit trails
  • CloudWatch Alarms: Proactive monitoring and alerting
  • CloudWatch Insights: Advanced log analysis
📝 CloudWatch Alarms for EFS
# Create alarm for high storage usage
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name "anihpj-efs-high-storage" \
    --alarm-description "Alert when EFS storage exceeds 100GB" \
    --metric-name StorageBytes \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --statistic Average \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --threshold 107374182400 \
    --period 3600 \
    --evaluation-periods 1 \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID Name=StorageClass,Value=Standard \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:account:anihpj-alerts

# Create alarm for performance issues
aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name "anihpj-efs-high-latency" \
    --alarm-description "Alert when EFS latency is high" \
    --metric-name TotalIOTime \
    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --statistic Average \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --threshold 100 \
    --period 300 \
    --evaluation-periods 2 \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:account:anihpj-alerts
🎯 Integration Best Practices:
  • Use Access Points to isolate different services and applications
  • Enable transit encryption for production workloads
  • Monitor performance metrics and set up appropriate alarms
  • Use IAM roles instead of hardcoded credentials for service access
  • Implement proper error handling and retry logic in applications

CloudFormation Template
📝 Complete EFS Stack
# anihpj-efs-stack.yml
AWSTemplateFormatVersion: '2010-09-09'
Description: 'Amazon EFS for anihpj job portal shared storage'

Parameters:
  VpcId:
    Type: AWS::EC2::VPC::Id
    Description: VPC ID where EFS will be deployed
  
  PrivateSubnetIds:
    Type: List
    Description: Private subnet IDs for mount targets
  
  EC2SecurityGroupId:
    Type: AWS::EC2::SecurityGroup::Id
    Description: Security group ID of EC2 instances

Resources:
  # EFS File System
  EFSFileSystem:
    Type: AWS::EFS::FileSystem
    Properties:
      CreationToken: !Sub 'anihpj-efs-${AWS::StackName}'
      PerformanceMode: generalPurpose
      ThroughputMode: bursting
      Encrypted: true
      FileSystemTags:
        - Key: Name
          Value: anihpj-shared-storage
        - Key: Environment
          Value: production
        - Key: Application
          Value: jobportal

  # Security Group for EFS
  EFSSecurityGroup:
    Type: AWS::EC2::SecurityGroup
    Properties:
      GroupDescription: Security group for anihpj EFS mount targets
      VpcId: !Ref VpcId
      SecurityGroupIngress:
        - IpProtocol: tcp
          FromPort: 2049
          ToPort: 2049
          SourceSecurityGroupId: !Ref EC2SecurityGroupId
          Description: NFS traffic from EC2 instances
      Tags:
        - Key: Name
          Value: anihpj-efs-sg

  # Mount Targets (one per AZ)
  MountTarget1:
    Type: AWS::EFS::MountTarget
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      SubnetId: !Select [0, !Ref PrivateSubnetIds]
      SecurityGroups:
        - !Ref EFSSecurityGroup

  MountTarget2:
    Type: AWS::EFS::MountTarget
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      SubnetId: !Select [1, !Ref PrivateSubnetIds]
      SecurityGroups:
        - !Ref EFSSecurityGroup

  # Access Points
  MediaAccessPoint:
    Type: AWS::EFS::AccessPoint
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      PosixUser:
        Uid: 1000
        Gid: 1000
      RootDirectory:
        Path: '/media'
        CreationInfo:
          OwnerUid: 1000
          OwnerGid: 1000
          Permissions: '755'
      AccessPointTags:
        - Key: Name
          Value: anihpj-media-access

  LogsAccessPoint:
    Type: AWS::EFS::AccessPoint
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      PosixUser:
        Uid: 1000
        Gid: 1000
      RootDirectory:
        Path: '/logs'
        CreationInfo:
          OwnerUid: 1000
          OwnerGid: 1000
          Permissions: '755'
      AccessPointTags:
        - Key: Name
          Value: anihpj-logs-access

  # Backup Policy
  EFSBackupPolicy:
    Type: AWS::EFS::BackupPolicy
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      BackupPolicy:
        Status: ENABLED

  # Lifecycle Policy
  EFSLifecyclePolicy:
    Type: AWS::EFS::LifecycleConfiguration
    Properties:
      FileSystemId: !Ref EFSFileSystem
      LifecyclePolicies:
        - TransitionToIA: AFTER_30_DAYS

Outputs:
  FileSystemId:
    Description: EFS File System ID
    Value: !Ref EFSFileSystem
    Export:
      Name: !Sub '${AWS::StackName}-FileSystemId'

  MediaAccessPointId:
    Description: Media Access Point ID
    Value: !Ref MediaAccessPoint
    Export:
      Name: !Sub '${AWS::StackName}-MediaAccessPointId'

  LogsAccessPointId:
    Description: Logs Access Point ID
    Value: !Ref LogsAccessPoint
    Export:
      Name: !Sub '${AWS::StackName}-LogsAccessPointId'

  EFSDNSName:
    Description: EFS DNS Name for mounting
    Value: !Sub '${EFSFileSystem}.efs.${AWS::Region}.amazonaws.com'
    Export:
      Name: !Sub '${AWS::StackName}-DNSName'

  type        = string

# EFS File System
resource "aws_efs_file_system" "anihpj_efs" {
  creation_token   = "anihpj-efs-${random_id.creation_token.hex}"
  performance_mode = "generalPurpose"
  throughput_mode  = "bursting"
  encrypted        = true

  lifecycle_policy {
    transition_to_ia = "AFTER_30_DAYS"
  }

  tags = {
    Name        = "anihpj-shared-storage"
    Environment = "production"
    Application = "jobportal"
  }
}

resource "random_id" "creation_token" {
  byte_length = 8
}

# Security Group for EFS
resource "aws_security_group" "efs_sg" {
  name_prefix = "anihpj-efs-"
  vpc_id      = var.vpc_id

  ingress {
    from_port       = 2049
    to_port         = 2049
    protocol        = "tcp"
    security_groups = [var.ec2_security_group_id]
    description     = "NFS traffic from EC2 instances"
  }

  egress {
    from_port   = 0
    to_port     = 0
    protocol    = "-1"
    cidr_blocks = ["0.0.0.0/0"]
  }

  tags = {
    Name = "anihpj-efs-sg"
  }
}

# Mount Targets
resource "aws_efs_mount_target" "anihpj_mount_targets" {
  count           = length(var.private_subnet_ids)
  file_system_id  = aws_efs_file_system.anihpj_efs.id
  subnet_id       = var.private_subnet_ids[count.index]
  security_groups = [aws_security_group.efs_sg.id]
}

🔄 CI/CD Pipeline Integration
📝 GitHub Actions with EFS
# .github/workflows/deploy-with-efs.yml
name: Deploy anihpj with EFS Storage

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
  pull_request:
    branches: [main]

env:
  AWS_REGION: us-east-1
  EFS_FILE_SYSTEM_ID: fs-12345678

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Set up Python
      uses: actions/setup-python@v4
      with:
        python-version: '3.11'
    
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: |
        python -m pip install --upgrade pip
        pip install -r requirements.txt
        pip install pytest pytest-django
    
    - name: Run tests
      run: pytest

  deploy-infrastructure:
    needs: test
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Configure AWS credentials
      uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v2
      with:
        aws-access-key-id: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        aws-secret-access-key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        aws-region: ${{ env.AWS_REGION }}
    
    - name: Deploy EFS CloudFormation Stack
      run: |
        aws cloudformation deploy \
          --template-file infrastructure/efs-stack.yml \
          --stack-name anihpj-efs-production \
          --parameter-overrides \
            VpcId=${{ secrets.VPC_ID }} \
            PrivateSubnetIds=${{ secrets.PRIVATE_SUBNET_IDS }} \
            EC2SecurityGroupId=${{ secrets.EC2_SG_ID }} \
          --capabilities CAPABILITY_IAM \
          --no-fail-on-empty-changeset

  deploy-application:
    needs: [test, deploy-infrastructure]
    runs-on: self-hosted  # EC2 instance with EFS mounted
    if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Install Python dependencies
      run: |
        source /opt/anihpj/venv/bin/activate
        pip install -r requirements.txt
    
    - name: Run database migrations
      run: |
        source /opt/anihpj/venv/bin/activate
        python manage.py migrate
    
    - name: Collect static files to EFS
      run: |
        source /opt/anihpj/venv/bin/activate
        # Collect to local directory first
        python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
        # Then sync to EFS for shared access
        rsync -av --delete staticfiles/ /mnt/efs/anihpj/static/
    
    - name: Deploy application code to EFS
      run: |
        # Deploy to shared EFS location
        rsync -av --delete \
          --exclude='.git/' \
          --exclude='__pycache__/' \
          --exclude='*.pyc' \
          . /mnt/efs/anihpj/code/
    
    - name: Restart application services
      run: |
        # Restart Django application (all instances will pick up changes)
        sudo systemctl restart anihpj-web
        sudo systemctl restart anihpj-workers
    
    - name: Health check
      run: |
        # Wait for application to start
        sleep 30
        # Check application health
        curl -f http://localhost:8000/health/ || exit 1
    
    - name: Log deployment
      run: |
        echo "$(date): Deployed commit $(git rev-parse HEAD) by ${{ github.actor }}" >> /mnt/efs/anihpj/logs/deployments.log

    command: celery -A anihpj worker -l info
    volumes:
      - type: bind
        source: /mnt/efs/anihpj/media
        target: /app/media
      - type: bind
        source: /mnt/efs/anihpj/logs
        target: /app/logs
    environment:
      - DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE=anihpj.settings.production
      - DATABASE_URL=postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj
    depends_on:
      - db
      - redis
    networks:
      - anihpj-network

  nginx:
    image: nginx:alpine
    ports:
      - "80:80"

      - /mnt/efs/anihpj/media:/usr/share/nginx/html/media:ro

    networks:
      - anihpj-network

  redis:
    image: redis:alpine
    networks:
      - anihpj-network

volumes:
  postgres_data:

networks:
  anihpj-network:
    driver: bridge
🎯 Deployment Best Practices:
  • Use Infrastructure as Code (CloudFormation/Terraform) for consistent deployments
  • Implement health checks and rollback mechanisms
  • Use EFS for shared application data, not for code deployment
  • Monitor deployment metrics and application performance post-deployment
  • Implement blue-green deployments for zero-downtime updates

Comprehensive Audit Trail:

  • CloudTrail: All EFS API calls logged
  • VPC Flow Logs: Network traffic to/from EFS
  • CloudWatch Logs: Application access patterns
  • AWS Config: Configuration change tracking
📝 Enable Comprehensive Logging
# Enable CloudTrail for EFS API calls
aws cloudtrail create-trail \
    --name anihpj-efs-audit-trail \
    --s3-bucket-name anihpj-audit-logs \
    --include-global-service-events \
    --is-multi-region-trail \
    --enable-log-file-validation

# Create Config rule for EFS encryption
aws configservice put-config-rule \
    --config-rule '{
        "ConfigRuleName": "efs-encrypted-check",
        "Description": "Checks whether Amazon EFS file systems are encrypted",
        "Source": {
            "Owner": "AWS",
            "SourceIdentifier": "EFS_ENCRYPTED_CHECK"
        }
    }'

# Enable VPC Flow Logs for EFS network traffic
aws ec2 create-flow-logs \
    --resource-type VPC \
    --resource-ids $VPC_ID \
    --traffic-type ALL \
    --log-destination-type cloud-watch-logs \
    --log-group-name /aws/vpc/flowlogs \
    --deliver-logs-permission-arn arn:aws:iam::account:role/flowlogsRole
🌍 GDPR & Privacy Compliance

GDPR Compliance Features:

  • Right to Erasure: Delete individual files or entire file systems
  • Data Portability: Export data using standard protocols
  • Data Processing Records: Audit trails for all data operations
  • Data Protection by Design: Encryption and access controls
📝 GDPR Compliance Script
# gdpr_compliance.py - GDPR data management for anihpj
import os
import shutil
import logging
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from pathlib import Path

class GDPRComplianceManager:
    def __init__(self, efs_mount_path='/mnt/efs/anihpj'):
        self.efs_path = Path(efs_mount_path)
        self.media_path = self.efs_path / 'media'
        self.audit_log = self.efs_path / 'logs' / 'gdpr_compliance.log'
        
        # Setup logging
        logging.basicConfig(
            filename=self.audit_log,
            level=logging.INFO,
            format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s'
        )
        self.logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
    
    def delete_user_data(self, user_id, reason="GDPR Right to Erasure"):
        """Delete all user data from EFS"""
        try:
            user_paths = [
                self.media_path / 'resumes' / str(user_id),
                self.media_path / 'profile_images' / str(user_id),
                self.media_path / 'company_logos' / str(user_id)
            ]
            
            deleted_files = []
            for path in user_paths:
                if path.exists():
                    if path.is_file():
                        path.unlink()
                        deleted_files.append(str(path))
                    elif path.is_dir():
                        shutil.rmtree(path)
                        deleted_files.append(str(path))
            
            # Log the deletion
            self.logger.info(f"GDPR Deletion - User ID: {user_id}, "
                           f"Reason: {reason}, Files: {deleted_files}")
            
            return {
                'success': True,
                'deleted_files': deleted_files,
                'timestamp': datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
            }
            
        except Exception as e:
            self.logger.error(f"GDPR Deletion Failed - User ID: {user_id}, "
                            f"Error: {str(e)}")
            return {'success': False, 'error': str(e)}
    
    def export_user_data(self, user_id, export_path):
        """Export user data for GDPR data portability"""
        try:
            export_dir = Path(export_path) / f"user_{user_id}_export"
            export_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
            
            # Find and copy user files
            user_files = []
            search_paths = [
                self.media_path / 'resumes' / str(user_id),
                self.media_path / 'profile_images' / str(user_id)
            ]
            
            for search_path in search_paths:
                if search_path.exists():
                    if search_path.is_file():
                        dest = export_dir / search_path.name
                        shutil.copy2(search_path, dest)
                        user_files.append(str(dest))
                    elif search_path.is_dir():
                        dest_dir = export_dir / search_path.name
                        shutil.copytree(search_path, dest_dir)
                        user_files.extend([str(f) for f in dest_dir.rglob('*') if f.is_file()])
            
            # Create data inventory
            inventory = {
                'user_id': user_id,
                'export_date': datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
                'files_exported': user_files,
                'total_files': len(user_files)
            }
            
            with open(export_dir / 'data_inventory.json', 'w') as f:
                import json
                json.dump(inventory, f, indent=2)
            
            self.logger.info(f"GDPR Export - User ID: {user_id}, "
                           f"Files: {len(user_files)}, Path: {export_dir}")
            
            return inventory
            
        except Exception as e:
            self.logger.error(f"GDPR Export Failed - User ID: {user_id}, "
                            f"Error: {str(e)}")
            return {'success': False, 'error': str(e)}
    
    def cleanup_old_data(self, retention_days=7*365):  # 7 years default
        """Cleanup old data based on retention policy"""
        cutoff_date = datetime.now() - timedelta(days=retention_days)
        cutoff_timestamp = cutoff_date.timestamp()
        
        cleaned_files = []
        
        for file_path in self.media_path.rglob('*'):
            if file_path.is_file():
                file_mtime = file_path.stat().st_mtime
                if file_mtime < cutoff_timestamp:
                    try:
                        file_path.unlink()
                        cleaned_files.append(str(file_path))
                    except Exception as e:
                        self.logger.error(f"Failed to delete old file {file_path}: {e}")
        
        self.logger.info(f"Data Retention Cleanup - Deleted {len(cleaned_files)} files "
                        f"older than {retention_days} days")
        
        return {
            'deleted_files': len(cleaned_files),
            'cutoff_date': cutoff_date.isoformat()
        }

# Usage example
if __name__ == '__main__':
    gdpr_manager = GDPRComplianceManager()
    
    # Example: Delete user data
    result = gdpr_manager.delete_user_data(user_id=123, reason="User requested deletion")
    print(f"Deletion result: {result}")
    
    # Example: Export user data
    export_result = gdpr_manager.export_user_data(user_id=456, export_path='/tmp/exports')
    print(f"Export result: {export_result}")
    
    # Example: Cleanup old data
    cleanup_result = gdpr_manager.cleanup_old_data(retention_days=2555)  # 7 years
    print(f"Cleanup result: {cleanup_result}")
⚠️ Compliance Considerations:
  • Implement data retention policies aligned with business requirements
  • Regular compliance audits and documentation updates
  • Staff training on data handling and privacy requirements
  • Incident response procedures for data breaches
  • Regular testing of data deletion and export procedures

Tools for measuring EFS performance

    --size=1G --ioengine=libaio --direct=1 --bs=4k \

    --namespace AWS/EFS \
    --metric-name StorageBytes \
    --dimensions Name=FileSystemId,Value=$EFS_ID \
    --start-time $(date -d '1 day ago' -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
    --end-time $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average

📖 Glossary

Access Point

An application-specific entry point into an EFS file system that makes it easier to manage application access to shared datasets.

Availability Zone (AZ)

A distinct location within an AWS Region that is engineered to be isolated from failures in other Availability Zones.

Backup Policy

A configuration that enables automatic backups of an EFS file system using AWS Backup service.

Bursting

The ability to burst to higher performance levels when file system size and burst credits allow.

Creation Token

A unique string that ensures idempotent file system creation and helps identify the file system.

Elastic Network Interface (ENI)

A virtual network interface in your VPC that EFS mount targets use to provide network access to the file system.

File System Policy

A resource-based policy that controls NFS client access to the EFS file system.

General Purpose

EFS performance mode optimized for latency-sensitive use cases, supporting up to 7,000 file operations per second.

Infrequent Access (IA)

A storage class for files that are not accessed every day, providing cost savings with slightly higher access latency.

Lifecycle Management

A feature that automatically moves files between Standard and Infrequent Access storage classes based on access patterns.

Max I/O

EFS performance mode that can achieve higher levels of aggregate throughput and operations per second (legacy).

Mount Target

A network endpoint that provides access to an EFS file system within a specific subnet and Availability Zone.

NFS (Network File System)

A distributed file system protocol that allows mounting of remote file systems over a network as if they were local.

NFS Utils

Traditional Linux NFS client tools used for mounting NFS file systems without encryption.

One Zone

EFS storage class that stores data redundantly within a single Availability Zone for cost optimization.

POSIX

Portable Operating System Interface - a set of standards for maintaining compatibility between operating systems.

Provisioned Throughput

A throughput mode that allows you to specify the throughput of your file system independent of storage size.

Regional

EFS storage class that stores data redundantly across multiple Availability Zones within a region.

Security Group

A virtual firewall that controls traffic to and from EFS mount targets at the instance level.

Standard

The default EFS storage class for frequently accessed files, providing the lowest latency per operation.

Throughput

The rate at which data can be transferred to and from the file system, typically measured in MB/s.

Transit Encryption

Encryption of data in transit between the client and EFS, using TLS 1.2 and stunnel.

VPC (Virtual Private Cloud)

A logically isolated section of AWS cloud where EFS file systems and mount targets are deployed.

🎯 Decision Matrix for anihpj
Choose EFS When:
  • ✅ Multiple EC2 instances need shared file access
  • ✅ Storing user-uploaded files (resumes, profile images)
  • ✅ Centralizing application logs across instances
  • ✅ Need POSIX-compliant file system operations
  • ✅ Elastic scaling without capacity planning
  • ✅ Cross-AZ high availability is required
  • ✅ Integration with Lambda for file processing
Choose EBS When:
  • ✅ High-performance database storage needed
  • ✅ Operating system and application binaries
  • ✅ Single instance exclusive access required
  • ✅ Consistent, low-latency performance needed
  • ✅ Snapshot-based backup requirements
  • ✅ Boot volumes for EC2 instances
Choose S3 When:
  • ✅ Static website assets (CSS, JS, images)
  • ✅ Long-term archival and backup storage
  • ✅ Content distribution via CloudFront
  • ✅ Data analytics and big data processing
  • ✅ Cost-effective storage for infrequent access
  • ✅ Integration with other AWS services
Choose FSx When:
  • ✅ Windows-based applications requiring SMB
  • ✅ High-performance computing workloads
  • ✅ Lustre file system for HPC applications
  • ✅ Sub-millisecond latencies required
  • ✅ Legacy applications with specific file system needs

💾 Amazon EBS (Elastic Block Store)

Category: Storage  |  Use Case: High-Performance Block Storage for EC2  |  Pricing: Pay-per-GB Provisioned + IOPS  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS EBS Docs

Amazon EBS provides high-performance block storage volumes for EC2 instances. Perfect for database storage, file systems, boot volumes, and any raw block-level storage needs for the anihpj Django application.

📋 Overview & Introduction

Amazon EBS (Elastic Block Store) is a high-performance block storage service designed for use with Amazon EC2. It provides persistent, high-performance block-level storage volumes that can be attached to running EC2 instances.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • High Performance: Up to 256,000 IOPS and 4,000 MB/s throughput per volume
  • Durability: 99.999% availability with automatic replication within AZ
  • Flexible: Dynamically increase volume size, performance, and change volume type
  • Secure: Encryption at rest and in transit with AWS KMS integration
  • Backup: Point-in-time snapshots stored in Amazon S3
  • Multi-Attach: Attach single volume to multiple EC2 instances
  • Cost-Effective: Multiple volume types optimized for different workloads
💡 Perfect for anihpj: Store Django application databases (PostgreSQL), handle media file storage, maintain application logs, and provide high-performance boot volumes for web servers.
🏗️ EBS Architecture for anihpj
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

🔧 Core Concepts

💾 EBS Volumes

EBS Volumes are virtual hard drives that attach to EC2 instances:

  • Block-Level Storage: Raw, unformatted block-level storage device
  • Single AZ: Volumes exist in specific Availability Zone
  • Persistent: Data persists independently of EC2 instance lifecycle
  • Flexible: Dynamically modify size, performance, and type
  • Encrypted: At-rest and in-transit encryption available
📊 Volume Types
🚀 gp3 (General Purpose SSD)
  • Use Case: Most workloads
  • Size: 1 GB - 16 TB
  • IOPS: 3,000-16,000
  • Throughput: 125-1,000 MB/s
  • anihpj: Web servers, logs
⚡ io2 (Provisioned IOPS SSD)
  • Use Case: I/O intensive
  • Size: 4 GB - 64 TB
  • IOPS: 100-256,000
  • Durability: 99.999%
  • anihpj: PostgreSQL database
📈 st1 (Throughput Optimized HDD)
  • Use Case: Big data, analytics
  • Size: 125 GB - 16 TB
  • Throughput: Up to 500 MB/s
  • Cost: Lowest per GB
  • anihpj: Log analytics, backups
💾 sc1 (Cold HDD)
  • Use Case: Infrequent access
  • Size: 125 GB - 16 TB
  • Throughput: Up to 250 MB/s
  • Cost: Lowest cost
  • anihpj: Archive storage
📝 Volume Type Selection for anihpj
# Root volume for web servers (gp3)
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --size 30 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --iops 3000 \
    --throughput 125 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-web-root},{Key=Environment,Value=production}]'

# Database volume (io2 for high performance)
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --size 500 \
    --volume-type io2 \
    --iops 10000 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1c \
    --encrypted \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-db-data},{Key=Environment,Value=production}]'

# Log analytics volume (st1 for throughput)
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --size 1000 \
    --volume-type st1 \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-analytics},{Key=Environment,Value=production}]'
📸 Snapshots

EBS Snapshots provide point-in-time backups:

  • Incremental: Only changed blocks since last snapshot
  • Cross-Region: Copy snapshots to other regions for DR
  • Encryption: Encrypted volumes create encrypted snapshots
  • Fast Restore: Pre-warm snapshots for faster volume creation
📊 Snapshot Lifecycle for anihpj
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    EBS Snapshot Strategy                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  🗃️ Production Database Volume (500GB io2)                      │
│  └─────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────── │
│            │                                                   │
│            ▼                                                   │
│  📅 Automated Snapshot Schedule                                │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  🌅 Daily: 2 AM UTC (7 day retention)                 │    │
│  │  📅 Weekly: Sunday 1 AM UTC (4 week retention)        │    │
│  │  🗓️ Monthly: 1st of month (12 month retention)       │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  🌍 Cross-Region Disaster Recovery                             │
│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  📍 Primary: us-east-1                                 │    │
│  │  📍 DR: us-west-2 (Weekly snapshots)                  │    │
│  │  ⚡ Fast Snapshot Restore enabled for critical volumes │    │
│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                 │
│  💰 Cost Optimization                                          │
│  └─ Lifecycle policy: Delete snapshots > 12 months old        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🔒 Encryption

EBS Encryption provides comprehensive data protection:

  • At Rest: Data encrypted on the volume using AES-256
  • In Transit: Data encrypted between EC2 and EBS
  • Snapshots: Encrypted volumes create encrypted snapshots
  • Key Management: AWS managed or customer managed KMS keys
🔗 Multi-Attach

Multi-Attach enables shared block storage:

  • Concurrent Access: Up to 16 EC2 instances per volume
  • Use Cases: Clustered databases, shared file systems
  • Limitations: Only io1, io2, and gp3 volume types
  • File System: Requires cluster-aware file system

🚀 Getting Started

📋 Prerequisites
  • ✅ AWS Account: Active AWS account with EC2 permissions
  • ✅ EC2 Instance: Running EC2 instance in target AZ
  • ✅ IAM Permissions: EC2 volume creation and attachment permissions
  • ✅ SSH Access: Access to EC2 instance for mounting
💾 Create EBS Volume
📝 Create Volume for anihpj Database
# Set environment variables
AVAILABILITY_ZONE="us-east-1a"
VOLUME_SIZE=500
VOLUME_TYPE="io2"
IOPS=10000

# Create encrypted EBS volume for anihpj database
VOLUME_ID=$(aws ec2 create-volume \
    --size $VOLUME_SIZE \
    --volume-type $VOLUME_TYPE \
    --iops $IOPS \
    --availability-zone $AVAILABILITY_ZONE \
    --encrypted \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[
        {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-database-volume},
        {Key=Environment,Value=production},
        {Key=Application,Value=anihpj-jobpost},
        {Key=Purpose,Value=postgresql-data}
    ]' \
    --query 'VolumeId' \
    --output text)

echo "Created EBS Volume: $VOLUME_ID"

# Wait for volume to be available
aws ec2 wait volume-available --volume-ids $VOLUME_ID
echo "Volume $VOLUME_ID is now available"
🔗 Attach Volume to EC2
📝 Attach Volume to anihpj Database Server
# Get EC2 instance ID for database server
INSTANCE_ID=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=tag:Name,Values=anihpj-database-server" \
              "Name=instance-state-name,Values=running" \
    --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].InstanceId' \
    --output text)

# Attach volume to instance
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id $VOLUME_ID \
    --instance-id $INSTANCE_ID \
    --device /dev/sdf

# Wait for attachment to complete
aws ec2 wait volume-in-use --volume-ids $VOLUME_ID

# Verify attachment
aws ec2 describe-volumes \
    --volume-ids $VOLUME_ID \
    --query 'Volumes[0].Attachments'
💿 Format and Mount Volume
📝 Format and Mount for PostgreSQL
# SSH into the EC2 instance and run these commands

# Check if volume is visible
lsblk

# Check if volume has a file system
sudo file -s /dev/nvme1n1

# If output shows 'data', volume needs formatting
# Format with ext4 for PostgreSQL
sudo mkfs -t ext4 /dev/nvme1n1

# Create mount point for PostgreSQL data
sudo mkdir -p /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Mount the volume
sudo mount /dev/nvme1n1 /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Set proper permissions for PostgreSQL
sudo chown -R postgres:postgres /var/lib/postgresql/data
sudo chmod 700 /var/lib/postgresql/data

# Add to fstab for persistent mounting
echo '/dev/nvme1n1 /var/lib/postgresql/data ext4 defaults,nofail 0 2' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab

# Verify mount
df -h /var/lib/postgresql/data
mount | grep nvme1n1

💾 Backup & Restore

Automated Snapshot Management ensures data protection:

  • Automated Backups: Schedule snapshots with AWS Backup or Lambda
  • Point-in-Time Recovery: Restore to any snapshot timestamp
  • Cross-Region Backup: Copy snapshots for disaster recovery
  • Fast Snapshot Restore: Pre-warm snapshots for instant volume creation
📝 Automated Backup for anihpj Database
# Create backup schedule using AWS CLI
aws backup create-backup-plan \
    --backup-plan '{
        "BackupPlanName": "anihpj-ebs-backup-plan",
        "Rules": [
            {
                "RuleName": "DailyBackup",
                "TargetBackupVault": "default",
                "ScheduleExpression": "cron(0 2 ? * * *)",
                "StartWindowMinutes": 60,
                "CompletionWindowMinutes": 120,
                "Lifecycle": {
                    "MoveToColdStorageAfterDays": 30,
                    "DeleteAfterDays": 365
                },
                "RecoveryPointTags": {
                    "Application": "anihpj",
                    "Environment": "production"
                }
            }
        ]
    }'

# Lambda function for custom snapshot logic
# lambda_backup.py
import boto3
import datetime
import json

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    ec2 = boto3.client('ec2')
    
    # Get all anihpj EBS volumes
    volumes = ec2.describe_volumes(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj-jobpost']},
            {'Name': 'state', 'Values': ['in-use']}
        ]
    )
    
    for volume in volumes['Volumes']:
        volume_id = volume['VolumeId']
        
        # Create snapshot
        snapshot = ec2.create_snapshot(
            VolumeId=volume_id,
            Description=f'Automated backup of {volume_id} - {datetime.datetime.now()}',
            TagSpecifications=[
                {
                    'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                    'Tags': [
                        {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': f'anihpj-auto-backup-{volume_id}'},
                        {'Key': 'Application', 'Value': 'anihpj-jobpost'},
                        {'Key': 'BackupType', 'Value': 'automated'},
                        {'Key': 'CreatedDate', 'Value': datetime.datetime.now().isoformat()}
                    ]
                }
            ]
        )
        
        print(f"Created snapshot {snapshot['SnapshotId']} for volume {volume_id}")
    
    return {
        'statusCode': 200,
        'body': json.dumps('Backup completed successfully')
    }

Dynamic Volume Modification allows scaling without downtime:

  • Size Increase: Expand volume size up to 64 TiB (io2) or 16 TiB (others)
  • IOPS Scaling: Increase IOPS for better performance
  • Volume Type Change: Migrate between volume types
  • Live Migration: No downtime required for most changes

    --size 1000 \
    --iops 15000 \

⚡ Fast Snapshot Restore (FSR)

Fast Snapshot Restore eliminates initialization latency:

  • Instant Access: Full performance immediately upon volume creation
  • Pre-warmed: Data blocks loaded into memory cache
  • Use Cases: Critical workloads, disaster recovery
  • Cost: $0.75 per DSU (Data Services Unit) per hour

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

💵 Pricing Model
gp3 (General Purpose)
$0.08/GB-month
  • 3,000 IOPS included
  • 125 MB/s throughput included
  • Extra IOPS: $0.005/IOPS-month
  • Extra throughput: $0.04/MB/s-month
io2 (Provisioned IOPS)
$0.125/GB-month
  • IOPS: $0.065/IOPS-month
  • 99.999% durability SLA
  • Best for critical workloads
  • Up to 256,000 IOPS
st1 (Throughput Optimized)
$0.045/GB-month
  • 500 MB/s throughput
  • Best for sequential I/O
  • Cannot be boot volume
  • 125 GB minimum size
sc1 (Cold HDD)
$0.025/GB-month
  • 250 MB/s throughput
  • Lowest cost option
  • Infrequent access workloads
  • 125 GB minimum size

#!/bin/bash

    --time-period Start=$(date -d "$(date +%Y-%m-01)" +%Y-%m-%d),End=$(date +%Y-%m-%d) \
    --granularity MONTHLY \

    --filters "Name=tag:Application,Values=anihpj-jobpost" \

    --log-group-name "/aws/ec2/cloudwatch" \
    --start-time $(date -d "7 days ago" +%s) \
    --end-time $(date +%s) \
    --query-string 'fields @timestamp, VolumeId, VolumeReadOps, VolumeWriteOps | filter VolumeId like /vol-/ | stats avg(VolumeReadOps), avg(VolumeWriteOps) by VolumeId'

🛡️ Disaster Recovery
📝 anihpj DR Implementation
# Cross-region disaster recovery setup
# Primary region: us-east-1, DR region: us-west-2

# 1. Copy critical snapshots to DR region
SNAPSHOT_ID="snap-0123456789abcdef0"
aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id $SNAPSHOT_ID \
    --destination-region us-west-2 \
    --description "anihpj DR backup - $(date)" \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=snapshot,Tags=[{Key=Purpose,Value=DisasterRecovery},{Key=Application,Value=anihpj}]'

# 2. Automated DR recovery script
#!/bin/bash
# dr-recovery.sh - Restore anihpj in DR region

DR_REGION="us-west-2"
SUBNET_ID="subnet-dr-12345"
SECURITY_GROUP="sg-dr-67890"

# Create volume from DR snapshot
VOLUME_ID=$(aws ec2 create-volume \
    --region $DR_REGION \
    --availability-zone us-west-2a \
    --snapshot-id $DR_SNAPSHOT_ID \
    --volume-type io2 \
    --iops 10000 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-dr-database}]' \
    --query 'VolumeId' \
    --output text)

# Launch DR instance from AMI
INSTANCE_ID=$(aws ec2 run-instances \
    --region $DR_REGION \
    --image-id $DR_AMI_ID \
    --instance-type m5.xlarge \
    --subnet-id $SUBNET_ID \
    --security-group-ids $SECURITY_GROUP \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-dr-database}]' \
    --query 'Instances[0].InstanceId' \
    --output text)

# Wait and attach volume
aws ec2 wait volume-available --volume-ids $VOLUME_ID --region $DR_REGION
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --region $DR_REGION \
    --volume-id $VOLUME_ID \
    --instance-id $INSTANCE_ID \
    --device /dev/sdf

echo "DR recovery initiated: Instance $INSTANCE_ID with volume $VOLUME_ID"

io2 Block Express provides the highest performance:

  • Maximum IOPS: Up to 256,000 IOPS per volume
  • Maximum Throughput: Up to 4,000 MB/s
  • Durability SLA: 99.999% annual durability
  • Sub-millisecond Latency: Consistent low latency

💿 RAID Configuration

RAID Arrays for Enhanced Performance:

  • RAID 0: Stripe multiple volumes for increased throughput
  • RAID 1: Mirror volumes for enhanced durability
  • RAID 10: Combine striping and mirroring
  • Use Cases: Exceed single volume limits, custom redundancy
📝 RAID 0 Setup for High Throughput
# Create multiple volumes for RAID 0 stripe
for i in {1..4}; do
    aws ec2 create-volume \
        --size 1000 \
        --volume-type gp3 \
        --iops 16000 \
        --throughput 1000 \
        --availability-zone us-east-1a \
        --tag-specifications "ResourceType=volume,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-raid0-vol${i}}]"
done

# Attach volumes to instance
# /dev/nvme1n1, /dev/nvme2n1, /dev/nvme3n1, /dev/nvme4n1

# Create RAID 0 array on EC2 instance
sudo mdadm --create /dev/md0 \
    --level=0 \
    --raid-devices=4 \
    /dev/nvme1n1 /dev/nvme2n1 /dev/nvme3n1 /dev/nvme4n1

# Format and mount
sudo mkfs.ext4 /dev/md0
sudo mkdir /mnt/raid0-storage
sudo mount /dev/md0 /mnt/raid0-storage

# Add to fstab
echo '/dev/md0 /mnt/raid0-storage ext4 defaults,nofail 0 2' | sudo tee -a /etc/fstab

# Performance result: ~4,000 MB/s throughput, 64,000 IOPS

⭐ Best Practices

🔒 Security Best Practices
1. Enable Encryption by Default
  • ✅ Enable EBS encryption by default in account settings
  • ✅ Use customer-managed KMS keys for sensitive data
  • ✅ Encrypt snapshots and AMIs containing sensitive data
  • ❌ Never store unencrypted sensitive data on volumes
2. Access Control & IAM
  • ✅ Use least privilege IAM policies for EBS operations
  • ✅ Implement resource-based tags for access control
  • ✅ Enable CloudTrail logging for EBS API calls
  • ✅ Use VPC endpoints for private API access
3. Network Security
  • ✅ Place volumes in private subnets when possible
  • ✅ Use security groups to restrict instance access
  • ✅ Monitor network traffic with VPC Flow Logs
  • ✅ Implement network ACLs for additional protection
⚡ Performance Best Practices
1. Volume Type Selection
  • ✅ Use gp3 for general workloads (cost-effective)
  • ✅ Use io2 for I/O intensive databases
  • ✅ Use st1 for sequential access patterns
  • ⚠️ Avoid io1 - io2 provides better value
2. IOPS and Throughput Optimization
# Optimize gp3 for anihpj database
aws ec2 modify-volume \
    --volume-id vol-1234567890abcdef0 \
    --iops 16000 \
    --throughput 1000

# Monitor queue depth and adjust
iostat -x 1 5  # Target queue depth < 32 for optimal latency
3. Application-Level Optimization
  • ✅ Use appropriate I/O block sizes (4KB-1MB)
  • ✅ Implement connection pooling for databases
  • ✅ Use read replicas to distribute read load
  • ✅ Cache frequently accessed data in memory
💾 Backup Best Practices
1. Automated Backup Strategy
# Lambda function for intelligent backup
import boto3
import datetime
import json

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    ec2 = boto3.client('ec2')
    
    # Get anihpj volumes needing backup
    volumes = ec2.describe_volumes(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj-jobpost']},
            {'Name': 'tag:BackupSchedule', 'Values': ['daily', 'weekly']}
        ]
    )
    
    for volume in volumes['Volumes']:
        backup_schedule = next(tag['Value'] for tag in volume['Tags'] 
                             if tag['Key'] == 'BackupSchedule')
        
        if should_backup(backup_schedule):
            create_snapshot(ec2, volume)
    
    # Cleanup old snapshots
    cleanup_old_snapshots(ec2)
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Backup completed'}

def should_backup(schedule):
    now = datetime.datetime.now()
    if schedule == 'daily':
        return True
    elif schedule == 'weekly':
        return now.weekday() == 6  # Sunday
    return False

def cleanup_old_snapshots(ec2):
    cutoff_date = datetime.datetime.now() - datetime.timedelta(days=30)
    
    snapshots = ec2.describe_snapshots(
        OwnerIds=['self'],
        Filters=[{'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj-jobpost']}]
    )
    
    for snapshot in snapshots['Snapshots']:
        start_time = snapshot['StartTime'].replace(tzinfo=None)
        if start_time < cutoff_date:
            ec2.delete_snapshot(SnapshotId=snapshot['SnapshotId'])
2. Backup Validation & Testing
  • ✅ Regularly test snapshot restore procedures
  • ✅ Validate data integrity after restore
  • ✅ Document recovery time objectives (RTO)
  • ✅ Monitor backup success rates with CloudWatch
3. Cross-Region Disaster Recovery
  • ✅ Copy critical snapshots to secondary region
  • ✅ Automate DR testing with scheduled procedures
  • ✅ Maintain infrastructure as code for rapid recovery
  • ✅ Document and practice failover procedures
🎯 anihpj Best Practice Summary:
  • Use encryption by default for all production volumes
  • Implement automated backup with 30-day retention
  • Monitor performance metrics and set up alerting
  • Use appropriate volume types for different workloads
  • Regular disaster recovery testing and documentation
  • Implement cost optimization through right-sizing

# PostgreSQL configuration for EBS optimization
# /etc/postgresql/13/main/postgresql.conf

# Data directory on io2 volume
data_directory = '/var/lib/postgresql/data'

# WAL logs on separate gp3 volume  
wal_directory = '/var/lib/postgresql/wal'

# Performance tuning for EBS
shared_buffers = '8GB'                    # 25% of RAM
effective_cache_size = '24GB'             # 75% of RAM
random_page_cost = 1.1                    # Optimized for SSD
effective_io_concurrency = 200            # For io2 volumes
checkpoint_completion_target = 0.9
wal_buffers = '64MB'
checkpoint_segments = 64

📝 Django Media Storage Configuration
# anihpj/settings.py
import os

# Media files on dedicated EBS volume
MEDIA_ROOT = '/var/lib/anihpj/media'  # Mounted gp3 volume
MEDIA_URL = '/media/'

# File upload settings optimized for EBS
FILE_UPLOAD_MAX_MEMORY_SIZE = 10 * 1024 * 1024  # 10MB
FILE_UPLOAD_TEMP_DIR = '/var/lib/anihpj/temp'    # Fast gp3 volume

# Custom storage for different file types
STORAGES = {
    'default': {
        'BACKEND': 'django.core.files.storage.FileSystemStorage',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'location': MEDIA_ROOT,
            'base_url': MEDIA_URL,
        }
    },
    'resumes': {
        'BACKEND': 'django.core.files.storage.FileSystemStorage',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'location': os.path.join(MEDIA_ROOT, 'resumes'),
            'base_url': f'{MEDIA_URL}resumes/',
        }
    }
}

# anihpj/jobpost/models.py
class JobApplication(models.Model):
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to='resumes/%Y/%m/',
        storage='resumes',  # Uses dedicated storage
        validators=[validate_file_size, validate_file_extension]
    )

Operating System and Application Boot:

  • Database Servers: gp3 root volumes with separate data volumes
  • Load Balancers: Small gp3 volumes for minimal OS requirements
  • Golden Images: Create AMIs from optimized boot volumes
📊 Big Data Analytics

Analytics and Data Processing:

  • Job Application Analytics: st1 volumes for processing application data
  • Log Analytics: st1 for analyzing web server and application logs
  • Data Warehouse: st1 for ETL processing and data storage
  • Machine Learning: Training data storage on cost-effective st1
📝 Analytics Pipeline with EBS
# analytics_processor.py
import pandas as pd
import os
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Process job application analytics on EBS st1 volume'
    
    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        # Analytics data stored on st1 volume for cost efficiency
        analytics_path = '/var/lib/anihpj/analytics'  # st1 mount point
        
        # Process application trends
        applications_df = pd.read_csv(f'{analytics_path}/applications.csv')
        
        # Generate insights
        monthly_trends = applications_df.groupby('month').agg({
            'application_count': 'sum',
            'success_rate': 'mean',
            'average_salary': 'mean'
        })
        
        # Store results back to st1 volume
        monthly_trends.to_csv(f'{analytics_path}/monthly_trends.csv')
        
        self.stdout.write('Analytics processing completed')

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

⚠️ Common Issues
🚨 Volume Attachment Failed

Symptoms: Cannot attach EBS volume to EC2 instance

Causes & Solutions:

  • ✅ Different AZ: Volume and instance must be in same AZ
  • ✅ Device Name Conflict: Use different device name (/dev/sdf, /dev/sdg)
  • ✅ Volume In Use: Check if volume is already attached elsewhere
  • ✅ Instance Limit: EC2 instance has maximum volume attachment limit
📝 Troubleshooting Commands
# Check volume status and availability zone
aws ec2 describe-volumes --volume-ids vol-1234567890abcdef0

# Check instance details and current attachments
aws ec2 describe-instances --instance-ids i-1234567890abcdef0

# List available device names
lsblk

# Force detach if stuck
aws ec2 detach-volume --volume-id vol-1234567890abcdef0 --force
⚡ Poor Performance

Symptoms: High latency, low IOPS, application slowness

Diagnosis & Solutions:

  • ✅ IOPS Limit: Check if hitting volume IOPS limits
  • ✅ Queue Depth: Monitor queue depth (should be < 32)
  • ✅ Instance Type: Ensure instance supports volume performance
  • ✅ Network Bandwidth: Check if hitting instance network limits
📝 Performance Diagnostic Commands
# Monitor real-time I/O performance
iostat -x 1 10

# Check queue depth and utilization
sar -d 1 5

# Monitor from CloudWatch
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EBS \
    --metric-name VolumeQueueLength \
    --dimensions Name=VolumeId,Value=vol-1234567890abcdef0 \
    --start-time $(date -d '1 hour ago' --iso-8601) \
    --end-time $(date --iso-8601) \
    --period 300 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum
💾 Snapshot Creation Issues

Symptoms: Snapshot fails or takes too long

Solutions:

  • ✅ High I/O Load: Reduce I/O during snapshot creation
  • ✅ Large Volume: First snapshot takes longer (full copy)
  • ✅ Permissions: Check IAM permissions for snapshot operations
  • ✅ Region Limits: Check snapshot limits in target region
⚡ Performance Issues
Symptom Possible Cause Solution Prevention
High Latency (>10ms) High queue depth Reduce concurrent I/O Right-size IOPS
Low IOPS gp2 burst credits exhausted Migrate to gp3 Monitor burst balance
Throughput Bottleneck Instance network limit Upgrade instance type Check instance specs
Application Timeouts I/O wait time high Increase volume IOPS Performance testing
🔗 Connectivity Issues
Volume Not Visible in OS
# Check if volume is attached at AWS level
aws ec2 describe-volumes --volume-ids vol-1234567890abcdef0

# Check block devices visible to OS
lsblk
sudo fdisk -l

# If using NVMe instances, check NVMe devices
sudo nvme list

# Rescan SCSI bus if needed
echo "- - -" | sudo tee /sys/class/scsi_host/host*/scan
❓ Frequently Asked Questions
Q: Can I attach one EBS volume to multiple EC2 instances?

A: Yes, but only with Multi-Attach enabled volumes (io1, io2, gp3). You need cluster-aware file systems like Amazon FSx or configure application-level coordination.

Q: What happens to my data if EC2 instance terminates?

A: EBS volumes persist independently. Root volumes delete by default but can be configured to persist. Additional volumes always persist unless explicitly deleted.

Q: How do I migrate from gp2 to gp3 without downtime?

A: Use elastic volume modification: aws ec2 modify-volume --volume-id vol-xxx --volume-type gp3. No downtime required for most cases.

Q: What's the maximum size for EBS volumes?

A: Depends on type: gp3/gp2/st1/sc1: 16 TiB, io1: 16 TiB, io2: 64 TiB, io2 Block Express: 256 TiB

Q: How are snapshots priced?

A: $0.05 per GB-month for incremental data stored. First snapshot is full copy, subsequent snapshots only store changed blocks.

    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --volume-type gp3

aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id snap-1234567890abcdef0 \
    --destination-region us-west-2 \
    --description "DR backup of anihpj database"

# Delete snapshot
aws ec2 delete-snapshot \
    --snapshot-id snap-1234567890abcdef0

    --volume-id vol-unencrypted \
    --description "Temp snapshot for encryption" \
    --query 'SnapshotId' \
    --output text)

aws ec2 create-volume \
    --snapshot-id $SNAPSHOT_ID \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --encrypted \
    --kms-key-id alias/anihpj-ebs-key
🐍 Python Boto3 Examples
📝 Complete EBS Management Class
import boto3
import time
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
import logging

class EBSManager:
    def __init__(self, region='us-east-1'):
        self.ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name=region)
        self.region = region
        self.logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)
    
    def create_volume(self, size, volume_type='gp3', az=None, 
                      encrypted=True, tags=None, iops=None):
        """Create EBS volume with anihpj defaults"""
        params = {
            'Size': size,
            'VolumeType': volume_type,
            'AvailabilityZone': az or f'{self.region}a',
            'Encrypted': encrypted
        }
        
        if volume_type in ['io1', 'io2'] and iops:
            params['Iops'] = iops
        
        if tags:
            params['TagSpecifications'] = [{
                'ResourceType': 'volume',
                'Tags': [{'Key': k, 'Value': v} for k, v in tags.items()]
            }]
        
        response = self.ec2.create_volume(**params)
        volume_id = response['VolumeId']
        
        self.logger.info(f"Created volume {volume_id}")
        return volume_id
    
    def wait_for_volume_available(self, volume_id, timeout=300):
        """Wait for volume to become available"""
        start_time = time.time()
        
        while time.time() - start_time < timeout:
            response = self.ec2.describe_volumes(VolumeIds=[volume_id])
            state = response['Volumes'][0]['State']
            
            if state == 'available':
                return True
            elif state == 'error':
                raise Exception(f"Volume {volume_id} is in error state")
            
            time.sleep(5)
        
        raise TimeoutError(f"Volume {volume_id} not available after {timeout}s")
    
    def attach_volume(self, volume_id, instance_id, device):
        """Attach volume to EC2 instance"""
        try:
            response = self.ec2.attach_volume(
                VolumeId=volume_id,
                InstanceId=instance_id,
                Device=device
            )
            self.logger.info(f"Attached {volume_id} to {instance_id} as {device}")
            return response
        except Exception as e:
            self.logger.error(f"Failed to attach volume: {e}")
            raise
    
    def create_snapshot(self, volume_id, description=None, tags=None):
        """Create snapshot with metadata"""
        desc = description or f"anihpj backup {datetime.now()}"
        
        params = {
            'VolumeId': volume_id,
            'Description': desc
        }
        
        if tags:
            params['TagSpecifications'] = [{
                'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                'Tags': [{'Key': k, 'Value': v} for k, v in tags.items()]
            }]
        
        response = self.ec2.create_snapshot(**params)
        snapshot_id = response['SnapshotId']
        
        self.logger.info(f"Created snapshot {snapshot_id} for volume {volume_id}")
        return snapshot_id
    
    def cleanup_old_snapshots(self, days_old=30, application='anihpj-jobpost'):
        """Delete snapshots older than specified days"""
        cutoff_date = datetime.now() - timedelta(days=days_old)
        
        snapshots = self.ec2.describe_snapshots(
            OwnerIds=['self'],
            Filters=[{
                'Name': 'tag:Application',
                'Values': [application]
            }]
        )
        
        deleted_count = 0
        for snapshot in snapshots['Snapshots']:
            if snapshot['StartTime'].replace(tzinfo=None) < cutoff_date:
                try:
                    self.ec2.delete_snapshot(SnapshotId=snapshot['SnapshotId'])
                    deleted_count += 1
                    self.logger.info(f"Deleted old snapshot {snapshot['SnapshotId']}")
                except Exception as e:
                    self.logger.error(f"Failed to delete snapshot: {e}")
        
        return deleted_count

# Usage example
if __name__ == "__main__":
    ebs = EBSManager()
    
    # Create database volume for anihpj
    volume_id = ebs.create_volume(
        size=500,
        volume_type='io2',
        iops=10000,
        tags={
            'Name': 'anihpj-database-volume',
            'Application': 'anihpj-jobpost',
            'Environment': 'production',
            'Purpose': 'postgresql-data'
        }
    )
    
    # Wait for availability and attach
    ebs.wait_for_volume_available(volume_id)
    ebs.attach_volume(volume_id, 'i-1234567890abcdef0', '/dev/sdf')

resource "aws_kms_key" "ebs_key" {
  description             = "anihpj EBS encryption key"
  deletion_window_in_days = 7

  tags = {
    Name        = "${var.application}-ebs-key"
    Environment = var.environment
  }
}

  name          = "alias/${var.application}-ebs"
  target_key_id = aws_kms_key.ebs_key.key_id
}

# Database volume (high performance)
resource "aws_ebs_volume" "database" {
  availability_zone = data.aws_availability_zones.available.names[0]
  size              = 500
  type              = "io2"
  iops              = 10000
  encrypted         = true
  kms_key_id        = aws_kms_key.ebs_key.arn

  tags = {
    Name        = "${var.application}-database-volume"
    Environment = var.environment
    Application = var.application
    Purpose     = "postgresql-data"

  }

  size              = 100

  iops              = 3000
  throughput        = 125
  encrypted         = true
  kms_key_id        = aws_kms_key.ebs_key.arn

    Environment = var.environment
    Application = var.application
    Purpose     = "web-server-storage"
  }

  availability_zone = data.aws_availability_zones.available.names[0]
  size              = 1000
  type              = "st1"
  encrypted         = true
  kms_key_id        = aws_kms_key.ebs_key.arn

  tags = {
    Name        = "${var.application}-analytics"
    Environment = var.environment
    Application = var.application
    Purpose     = "big-data-processing"
  }
}

# Snapshot lifecycle policy
resource "aws_dlm_lifecycle_policy" "ebs_backup" {
  description        = "anihpj EBS backup policy"
  execution_role_arn = aws_iam_role.dlm_lifecycle_role.arn
  state              = "ENABLED"

  policy_details {
    resource_types   = ["VOLUME"]
    target_tags = {
      Application = var.application
    }

    schedule {
      name = "Daily snapshots"

      create_rule {
        interval      = 24
        interval_unit = "HOURS"
        times         = ["02:00"]
      }

      retain_rule {
        count = 7
      }

      copy_tags = true

      tags_to_add = {
        SnapshotCreator = "DLM"
        Environment     = var.environment
      }
    }

    schedule {
      name = "Weekly snapshots"

      create_rule {
        cron_expression = "cron(0 1 ? * SUN *)"
      }

      retain_rule {
        count = 4
      }

      copy_tags = true
    }
  }
}

# IAM role for DLM
resource "aws_iam_role" "dlm_lifecycle_role" {
  name = "${var.application}-dlm-lifecycle-role"

  assume_role_policy = jsonencode({
    Version = "2012-10-17"
    Statement = [
      {
        Action = "sts:AssumeRole"
        Effect = "Allow"
        Principal = {
          Service = "dlm.amazonaws.com"
        }
      }
    ]
  })
}

resource "aws_iam_role_policy_attachment" "dlm_lifecycle_policy" {
  role       = aws_iam_role.dlm_lifecycle_role.name
  policy_arn = "arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/service-role/AWSDataLifecycleManagerServiceRole"
}

# Data sources
data "aws_availability_zones" "available" {
  state = "available"
}

🗃️ RDS Integration

EBS as Backend Storage for RDS:

  • Storage Types: RDS uses EBS gp2, gp3, io1, io2 under the hood
  • Storage Scaling: RDS storage scaling uses EBS elastic volumes
  • Backup Integration: RDS snapshots leverage EBS snapshot technology
  • Performance: RDS IOPS directly correlate to EBS IOPS
📊 RDS vs Self-Managed PostgreSQL on EBS
Aspect Amazon RDS Self-Managed on EBS anihpj Recommendation
Management Fully managed Manual configuration RDS for simplicity
Cost (500GB) ~$400/month ~$150/month Self-managed for cost
Control Limited Full control Self-managed for flexibility
Backups Automated Manual setup RDS advantage
⚡ Lambda Integration

EFS for Lambda Persistent Storage (EBS Not Directly Supported):

  • Limitation: Lambda cannot directly access EBS volumes
  • Alternative: Use EFS for shared persistent storage with Lambda
  • Data Processing: Lambda can process EBS snapshots in S3
  • Automation: Lambda functions for EBS management tasks
📝 Lambda Function for EBS Snapshot Management
# lambda_ebs_manager.py
import boto3
import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """
    Automated EBS snapshot management for anihpj
    Triggered by CloudWatch Events (cron schedule)
    """
    ec2 = boto3.client('ec2')
    
    # Create snapshots for anihpj volumes
    volumes = ec2.describe_volumes(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj-jobpost']},
            {'Name': 'tag:BackupSchedule', 'Values': ['daily']},
            {'Name': 'state', 'Values': ['in-use']}
        ]
    )
    
    created_snapshots = []
    
    for volume in volumes['Volumes']:
        volume_id = volume['VolumeId']
        
        # Get volume name for snapshot description
        volume_name = next(
            (tag['Value'] for tag in volume['Tags'] if tag['Key'] == 'Name'),
            volume_id
        )
        
        # Create snapshot
        response = ec2.create_snapshot(
            VolumeId=volume_id,
            Description=f'Automated backup of {volume_name} - {datetime.now()}',
            TagSpecifications=[{
                'ResourceType': 'snapshot',
                'Tags': [
                    {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': f'{volume_name}-backup-{datetime.now().strftime("%Y%m%d")}'},
                    {'Key': 'Application', 'Value': 'anihpj-jobpost'},
                    {'Key': 'CreatedBy', 'Value': 'Lambda-Automation'},
                    {'Key': 'RetentionDays', 'Value': '7'}
                ]
            }]
        )
        
        created_snapshots.append({
            'VolumeId': volume_id,
            'SnapshotId': response['SnapshotId'],
            'VolumeName': volume_name
        })
    
    # Clean up old snapshots
    cleanup_old_snapshots(ec2)
    
    return {
        'statusCode': 200,
        'body': json.dumps({
            'message': f'Created {len(created_snapshots)} snapshots',
            'snapshots': created_snapshots
        })
    }

def cleanup_old_snapshots(ec2):
    """Remove snapshots older than retention period"""
    cutoff_date = datetime.now() - timedelta(days=7)
    
    snapshots = ec2.describe_snapshots(
        OwnerIds=['self'],
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Application', 'Values': ['anihpj-jobpost']},
            {'Name': 'tag:CreatedBy', 'Values': ['Lambda-Automation']}
        ]
    )
    
    for snapshot in snapshots['Snapshots']:
        if snapshot['StartTime'].replace(tzinfo=None) < cutoff_date:
            try:
                ec2.delete_snapshot(SnapshotId=snapshot['SnapshotId'])
                print(f"Deleted old snapshot: {snapshot['SnapshotId']}")
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"Error deleting snapshot {snapshot['SnapshotId']}: {e}")
